The BSN program provides an intensive nursing practicum that will refine further the nursing competencies to ensure achievement of the BSN program outcomes required of an entry level nurse.

The BSN program aims to develop a professional nurse who is able to assume entry level positions in health facilities or community settings. The professional nurse is capable of providing safe, humane, quality and holistic care to individuals in varying age, gender and health−illness status; healthy or at−risk families; population groups; and community; singly or in collaboration with or other health care providers to promote health, prevent illness, restore health, alleviate suffering and provide end of life care. A Bachelor of Science in Nursing graduates shall:

5.1.1.	Apply knowledge of physical, social, natural and health sciences and humanities in the practice of nursing;
 
5.1.2.	Provide safe, appropriate and holistic care to individuals, families, population groups, and community utilizing nursing process;
5.1.3.	Apply guidelines and principles of evidence−based practice in the delivery of care;
5.1.4.	Practice nursing in accordance with existing laws, legal, ethical, and moral principles;
5.1.5.	Communicate effectively in speaking, writing and presenting using culturally−appropriate language;
5.1.6.	Report and document up−to−date client care accurately and comprehensively;
5.1.7.	Work effectively in collaboration with inter−, intra−, and multi−disciplinary and multi−cultural teams;
5.1.8.	Practice beginning management and leadership skills using systems approach in the delivery of client care;
5.1.9.	Conduct research with an experienced researcher;
5.1.10.	Engage in lifelong learning with a passion to keep current with national and global developments in general, and nursing and health developments in particular;
5.1.11.	Demonstrate responsible citizenship and pride in being a Filipino;
5.1.12.	Apply techno−intelligent care systems and processes in health care delivery;
5.1.13.	Adopt the nursing core values in the practice of the profession; and
5.1.14.	Apply entrepreneurial skills in the delivery of nursing care.

5.2.	Bachelor of Science in Midwifery (BSM)
The Bachelor of Science in Midwifery aims to develop higher level competencies of a midwife as a health care provider: educator, researcher, supervisor and health care facility manager/entrepreneur.

Specifically, this enables the graduates to give the necessary supervision, care and advice to high−risks parturient; execute emergency measures in the absence of medical practitioners; provide family planning services; provide Integrated Management of Childhood Illness (IMCI) services; manage MCH clinics at the community level; facilitate community organizing and social mobilization for community development; engage in independent,  entrepreneurial  health  activities  including
 
management of primary health care facilities; implement/manage midwifery programs; perform other health related functions as may be deemed necessary by appropriate agency. A Four− year Midwifery graduates shall:

5.2.1.	Exercise legal principles and code of ethics in making personal and professional judgment;
5.2.2.	Utilizes Primary Health Care in the delivery of health care services in the community and promotes safe quality care;
5.2.3.	Establishes collaborative relationship with colleagues and other members of the team to enhance midwifery practice and other health care services;
5.2.4.	Promotes professional and personal growth and development
5.2.5.	Engages in health−related researches for the development of midwifery practice;
5.2.6.	Demonstrates management and leadership skills to provide safe and quality care for mother and child;
5.2.7.	Exhibit a God centered midwives, responsible stewards of environment, mediator for cultural preservation and promotion;
5.2.8.	Manages a community/village−based health facility/component of a health program or health service; and
5.2.9.	Utilizes appropriate mechanism for networking linkage building and referrals.

5.3.	Diploma in Midwifery
The Diploma in Midwifery aims to develop the knowledge, attitude and skills of first level midwives in the care of the girl− child, the adolescent, and the adult woman prior to, during, and following pregnancy. This prepares the midwives to give the necessary supervision, care and advice to women during pregnancy, labor and post−partum period; manage normal deliveries on her own responsibility and care for the child.
 
Specifically, graduates of the 2−year program are expected to perform primary health care services within the community (promotive and preventive care); counsel and educate women, family and community regarding family planning including preparation for parenthood/parenting; detect abnormal conditions in the mother and infant; procure specialized assistance as necessary (consultation or referral). The graduates of this program should be able to:

5.3.1.	Provide necessary supervision, care and advises to normal women during pregnancy, labor and puerperium;
5.3.2.	Performs primary health care services within the community.
5.3.3.	Participate in researches related to midwifery practice.;
5.3.4.	Work independently or collaboratively with other health team imbued with core values of Midwifery practice;
5.3.5.	Practice professionalism and Filipino values with respect to individual and cultural diversity;
5.3.6.	Participate in professional Continuing Education thru attending seminars and trainings locally and internationally; and
5.3.7.	Use effective communication skills, both in writing and speaking using culturally appropriate language;
5.4.	Bachelor of Science in Radiologic Technology (BSRT)

The Bachelor of Science in Radiologic Technology program aims to produce radiologic technologists who are imbued with 21st century skills and are competent to fulfill professional responsibilities in the following area: diagnostic and therapeutic imaging, radiation safety and protection, patient care, administration and management, education, research, entrepreneurship, and life−long learning. Graduates of BSRT shall:

5.4.1.	Apply scientific knowledge, technical skills, and the proper work attitude and values necessary for the practice of Radiologic Technology;
5.4.2.	Understand the scope of local and international professional ethical practice;
 
5.4.3.	Promote the value of pursuing life−long learning;
5.4.4.	Implement radiation safety and protection measures;
5.4.5.	Demonstrate compassionate patient care;
5.4.6.	Show	beginning	leadership,	management,	and entrepreneurial skills;
5.4.7.	Engage in academic and research activities; and
5.4.8.	Advocate love of country and service to the Filipino people.

5.5.	Bachelor of Science in Medical Laboratory Science (BSMLS)
The BS in Medical Laboratory Science program provides the students’ foundation in the fundamentals of medical laboratory science, scientific concepts and principles of the different laboratory analyses and determinations to develop skills in critically analyzing laboratory processes. It trains students to be globally competent and knowledgeable in the performance of laboratory test procedures and analyses which aids in the diagnosis, treatment of diseases and maintenance of health. The program also provides a profound training and updates on various laboratory screening and examinations, scientific research, instrumentations, and community related activities. The students are developed to become well−rounded medical laboratory scientists. Graduate of BSMLS shall:
5.5.1.	Demonstrate technical competence in the performance of clinical laboratory tests in aid of diagnosis, treatment, and management of diseases vis−à−vis biosafety and waste management;
5.5.2.	Demonstrate analytical and critical thinking skills in the workplace;
5.5.3.	Engage in the collection, analysis, and projection of health information for improving the health care management system;
5.5.4.	Demonstrate interpersonal skills, leadership qualities, and ethical practice of the profession;
5.5.5.	Apply research skills in relevant areas of Medical Technology/Medical Laboratory Science practice;
5.5.6.	Participate in community−oriented activities.
5.5.7.	Engage in life−long learning activities; and
5.5.8.	Demonstrate effective teaching and communication skills.

6.8.	Bachelor of Science in Criminology (BSCrim)
The field of criminology is the study of crime and the various agencies of justice as they operate and react to crime, criminals and victims. It aims to provide the community with professionally competent and morally upright graduates who can deliver efficient and effective services in crime prevention, crime detection and investigation, law enforcement, public safety, custody and rehabilitation of offenders, criminal research among others. A graduate of BSC should be able to:

6.8.1.	Conduct criminological research on crimes, crime causation, victims and offenders to include deviant behavior;
6.8.2.	Internalize the concepts of human rights and the victim welfare;
6.8.3.	Demonstrate competence and broad understanding in law enforcement administration, public safety and criminal justice;
6.8.4.	Utilize criminalistics or forensic science in the investigation and detection of crime;
6.8.5.	Apply the principles and jurisprudence of criminal law, evidence and criminal procedure; and
6.8.6.	Ensure offenders rehabilitation, welfare, development, and re−integration to the community.
 
6.9.	Bachelor of Science in Computer Science (BSCS)

The program prepares students to design and create algorithmically complex software and develop new and effective algorithms for solving computing problems. A Computer Science graduate prepares to become an IT professional and researcher, proficient in designing and developing computing solutions, specifically in terms of:

6.9.4.	Research in Computer Science related areas; and
6.9.5.	Integration of knowledge learned in different areas of Computer Science.

6.10.	Bachelor of Secondary Education major in English (BSEd - English)
6.10.1.	Possess broad knowledge of language and literature for effective learning;
6.10.2.	Use English as a global language in a multilingual context as it applies to the teaching of language and literature;
6.10.3.	Acquire extensive reading background in language, literature, and allied fields;
6.10.4.	Demonstrate proficiency in oral and written communication;
 
6.10.5.	Shows competence in employing innovative language and literature teaching approaches, methodologies, and strategies;
6.10.6.	Use technology in facilitating language learning and teaching;
6.10.7.	Inspire student and colleagues to lead relevant and transformative changes to improve learning and teaching language and literature; and
6.10.8.	Display skills and abilities to be reflective and research− oriented language and literature teacher.

6.11.	Bachelor of Secondary Education major in Filipino (BSEd - Filipino)
6.11.1.	Nagpapamalas ng mataas na antas ng kaalaman sa pagtuturo ng wika at panitikang Filipino;
6.11.2.	Nagpapakita ng malawak at malalim na pag−unawa at kaalaman sa ugnayan ng wika, kultura, at lipunan;
6.11.3.	Nakagagamit ng iba−t ibang kasanayan at kaalaman sa proseso ng patuturo−pagkatuto;
6.11.4.	Nagtataglay ng kaalaman hinggil sa usapin ng Kultural at linggwistikang dibersidad ng bansa;
6.11.5.	Nakapagdidisenyo ng malikhain, inobatibo at integratibong mga alternatibong dulog sa patututo at pagkatuto; at
6.11.6.	Nakagagawa ng pananaliksik ukol sa ikauunlad ng wikang Filipino bilang wikang panturo;
6.12.	Bachelor of Science in Information Technology (BSIT).
The program prepares graduates to address various user needs involving the selection, development, application, integration and management of computing technologies within an organization. Moreover, BSIT graduates are expected to become globally competent, innovative, and socially and ethically responsible computing professionals engaged in life− long learning endeavors. They are capable of contributing to the country’s national development goals. Hence, they should have the ability to:
6.12.1.	Analyze complex problems, and identify and define the computing requirements needed to design an appropriate solution;
 
6.12.2.	Apply computing and other knowledge domains to address real−world problems;
6.12.3.	Design and develop computing solutions using a system−level perspective;
6.12.4.	Utilize modern computing tool;
6.12.5.	Articulate and discuss the latest developments in the specific field of practice;
6.12.6.	Effectively communicate orally and in writing using both English and Filipino;
6.12.7.	Work	effectively	and	independently	in	multi− disciplinary and multi−cultural teams;
6.12.8.	Act in recognition of professional, social, and ethical responsibly; and
6.12.9.	Preserve and promote “Filipino historical and cultural heritage”.

6.13.	Bachelor of Technical-Vocational Teacher Education (BTVTEd) BTVTEd program aims to develop knowledge, skills, and attitude necessary to prepare student to be a highly competent and motivated technical and vocational educator in Grade 9−10 TLE subjects, Senior High School Tech−Voc Livelihood Track subjects, TVET Training Courses, and Higher Education Technical and Education Courses. A graduate of BTVTEd should be able to:

a.	Effectively synthesize organized knowledge to allow analytical and critical thinking;
b.	Promote and facilitate efficiently and effectively learnings to enable learners to develop their potential to the fullest for a continuing pursuit of lifelong learning;
c.	be a committed humanist who has a clear understanding and appreciation of human ideals and values inspire learners to realize their potential;
d.	stand as a model teacher with high regard for learning imbued with proper work attitude and values as practiced in industry; and
e.	be able to Implement of TVTE innovative approach/insights, best practice in the context of K−12 TVL track.
 
6.13.1.	Bachelor of Technical-Vocational Teacher Education Major in Automotive Technology (BTVTEd-AT)
a.	Articulate the rootedness of education in philosophical, socio − cultural, historical, psychological, and political contexts;
b.	Articulate mastery on Training Regulations and Competency−Based Curriculum with focus Automotive Technology;
c.	Demonstrate mastery of on skills in Automotive Technology;
d.	Facilitate learning using a wide range of teaching methodologies appropriate to specific learners and their environments with focus on the skills recommended in Technical Vocational Education Trainer’s Methodology;
e.	Develop innovative curricula, instructional plans, teaching approaches, and resources for diverse learners with focus on the development of Competency−Based Curriculum and Competency− Based Learning Materials in Technical−Vocational Education;
f.	Apply skills in the development and utilization of ICT to promote quality, relevant, and sustainable educational practices;
g.	Demonstrate a variety of thinking skills in planning, monitoring, assessing and reporting learning processes and outcomes;
h.	Practice professional and ethical teaching standards responding to community, national, and global needs and realities; and
i.	Pursue lifelong learning for personal and professional growth through varied experiential and field–based opportunities.
 
6.13.2.	Bachelor of Technical-Vocational Teacher Education major in Food and Service Management (BTVTEd - FSM)
a.	Articulate the rootedness of education in philosophical, socio − cultural, historical, psychological, and political contexts;
b.	Articulate mastery on Training Regulations and Competency−Based Curriculum with focus Food Service Management;
c.	Demonstrate mastery of on skills in Food Service Management;
d.	Facilitate learning using a wide range of teaching methodologies appropriate to specific learners and their environments with focus on the skills recommended in Technical Vocational Education Trainer’s Methodology;
e.	Develop innovative curricula, instructional plans, teaching approaches, and resources for diverse learners with focus on the development of Competency−Based Curriculum and Competency− Based Learning Materials in Technical−Vocational Education;
f.	Apply skills in the development and utilization of ICT to promote quality, relevant, and sustainable educational practices;
g.	Demonstrate a variety of thinking skills in planning, monitoring, assessing and reporting learning processes and outcomes;
h.	Practice professional and ethical teaching standards responding to community, national, and global needs and realities; and
i.	Pursue lifelong learning for personal and professional growth through varied experiential and field–based opportunities.

B.	ACADEMIC STANDARDS AND REGULATIONS
1.	General Standards

1.1.	A student who wishes to enroll first year in any of the following College programs must have obtained the following ratings:

STATUS	OLSAT or Its Equivalent
Regular	At least High Average
Probationary	At least Low Average
1.2.	A student who gets probationary status based on the above ratings will be subjected to bridging program according to his/her deficient subject(s);
1.3.	A student who has failure/s shall be placed on academic probation and shall be deloaded correspondingly or redirected as determined by the Program Head and/or Dean of College;
 
1.4.	A student who drops a subject after Midterm or Third Quarterly is marked Dropped. However, if he/she gets a failing mark and drops before the final examination he/she is marked 5.0 (failed);
1.5.	A student must follow the curriculum of the college he/she is enrolled in.
1.6.	A student is encouraged to carry the normal semestral load as listed in the curriculum for each program;
1.7.	A 60% cut−off is the basis for all students' examinations using the approved transmutation table. However, a specific program may impose certain cut−off for their students to follow in order to remain in that program;
1.8.	The College encourages the students' participation in extra− curricular activities as supplementary activities for classroom instructions and for their holistic development. However, they have to make sure that these activities will not interfere with their academic studies; and
1.9.	The summer session is offered to cater to specific needs of the students. The maximum load is nine (9) units.
2.	Specific Standards

2.1.	COLLEGE OF EDUCATION, ARTS AND SCIENCES (CEDAS)

2.1.1.	Teacher Education Program
A student who wishes to enroll first year in the Teacher Education Program must follow the following policies:
a.	A senior high school graduate of any strand may enrol in the Teacher Education Program;
b.	A first−year student of the Teacher Education Program will be allowed to continue in the second−year program unless he/she has no failing grades or below the cut−off grade exceeding 15 units;
c.	A student who failed or has grades below the cut−off in three subjects or 9 units will be given first warning. A second warning will be given if he/she has already accumulated 12 units of failed subjects or below the cut−off grade. He/she will be automatically out from the program if he/she has already accumulated 15 units of failed subjects or below the cut−off grades; and
 
d.	All students must strictly follow the prerequisite subjects; otherwise, the enrolled subjects will be given no credit.

RETENTION SCHEME
a.	The cut−off grades for general education, professional, and major subjects shall be 2.5;
b.	The earned grades in the level will be accumulated as the student proceeds to the next year level.;
c.	An accumulation of 9 units (3 subjects of 3 units or any of the 1 or 2 units subjects) with grades below the cut− off or failed subjects shall be given the first warning and shall be subjected to academic counseling;
d.	An accumulation of 12 units (4 subjects of 3 units or any of the 1 or 2 units subjects) with grades below the cut− off or failed subjects shall be given the second warning and shall be subjected to intervention;
e.	An accumulation of 15 units (5 subjects of 3 units or any of the 1 or 2 unit subjects) with grades below the cut− off or failed subjects shall be subjected for redirection; and
f.	This scheme only applies until first semester of third year level only.
2.1.2.	Psychology Program
a.	A first−year student who fails in one (1) major subject during the semester will be required to report for counseling and participate in the mentoring program to facilitate his/her deficiencies. If the same students fail again in his/her subjects in the next semester or during summer, he/she automatically redirected to another program;
b.	A regular student who fails in (2) major subjects in second year or third year will not be allowed to take the requisite subjects until he/she passed the subject with the grade of 2.5 and he/she will be required to participate the mentoring program; and
c.	The basis for cut−off computation of grade is 60% in both minor and major examinations.
 
2.1.3.	Criminology Program
A student who wishes to enrol in the Criminology Program must follow the following policies:
a.	A Senior Highschool graduate of any strand can enroll in the Criminology Program;
b.	All students including returnees, transferees, shiftees and cross enrollees who wish to enroll in BS Criminology shall submit drug test result as requirement for enrolment.

RETENTION SCHEME
a.	A criminology student must maintain a grade of at least 80 or 2.5 in all his/her major subjects enrolled both in the first and second semester;
b.	A Criminology student is allowed to continue in the second−year program if he/she has accumulated the required cut− off 15 units of below 2.5 grade needed to be maintained in all of his/her major subjects;
c.	A Criminology student who failed or has grades below cut−off in three Subjects or 9 units will be given first warning. A second warning will be given for a total of 12 units below cut−off or failing grades;
d.	A Criminology student is advised to shift or will be redirected to another program if he/she has already reached the 15−unit limit accumulated grade of below 2.5;
e.	This scheme will only apply until first semester of third year level; and
f.	All students must strictly follow the pre−requisite subjects, otherwise the enrolled subjects will be given no credit.
2.2.	COLLEGE	OF	ACCOUNTANCY,	BUSINESS,	AND ENTREPRENEURSHIP (CABE)
2.2.1.	Bachelor of Science in Accountancy (BSA)
a.	An ABM CJC graduate who obtains a Grade Point Average (GPA) of 80 and above will be admitted to the BSA program without need to take the entrance exam. Those
 
with GPA below 80 will be redirected to other business programs;
b.	An ABM CJC graduate, a non CJC ABM graduate or a non CJC non−ABM graduate will take the entrance exam. A passing rate of 50% and above in specialized area will qualify the student to be admitted to the BSA program. Those who obtain a rate of below 50% will be admitted under probationary status for 1 semester only;
c.	A General Weighted Average (GWA) of 2.0 for the entire school year, with no grade below 2.7 in any subject, will qualify the student to be promoted to the next year level under the BSA program. Those who do not qualify will be redirected to other business programs. This applies from second year to fourth year level;
d.	For transferees and returnees, the program head will evaluate the subjects already taken to determine the year level in which the student qualifies. In cases when the transferee or returnee does not meet the school year evaluation requirement, the program head can intervene by placing the student in a temporary admission to the BSA program with an irregular probationary status;
e.	Students under probationary status must get a GWA of
2.0 for the semester, with no grade below 2.7 in any subject. The student must be enroled at least a minimum of 21 units in a semester. Those who do not qualify will be redirected to other business programs;
f.	Only graduating students are allowed to take a maximum of thirty (30) units; and
g.	The student must be able to obtain a National Certificate (NC) as a requirement before he/she can graduate of the program.

Grade Point Average (GPA) is the average grade of the Senior High School graduate from Grade 11 to Grade 12.

General Weighted Average (GWA) is the weighted average grade of the College student for the entire school year, excluding summer classes.
 
2.2.2.	Bachelor of Science in Accounting Information System (BSAIS)
a.	An ABM CJC graduate will be automatically admitted to the BSAIS program after taking the entrance exam;
b.	A non−ABM CJC graduate, a non−CJC ABM graduate or a non−CJC non−ABM graduate will be admitted after taking the entrance exam and interview. The interview will be conducted by the program head;
c.	Only graduating students are allowed to take a maximum of thirty (30) units;
d.	The total number of units and the subjects a student may register in a semester shall be in accordance with what is stipulated in the curricular program the student is enrolled in.
e.	Any student may be allowed to carry an overload of not more than 6 units provided, that such are back subjects;
f.	The arrangement of subjects in the curriculum of the course must be strictly followed. A student (1st year to 3rd year) who is enrolled in a subject without passing its prerequisite shall not be given academic credit;
g.	A graduating student may enroll in two subjects simultaneously, one of which is a prerequisite to the other, provided he/she does not exceed the maximum of 30 units as certified by his/her program head;
h.	A student should not have failed 2 times in the same subject. The total number of failed subjects should not be more than 3 subjects per semester; and
i.	A warning will be issued by the program head to a student who failed to comply with the above provision and will be advised to take tutorial classes. A student issued with 3 warnings will be redirected to other programs;
2.2.3.	Bachelor of Science in Management Accounting (BSMA)
a.	An ABM CJC graduate will be automatically admitted to the BSMA program after taking the entrance exam;
b.	A non−ABM CJC graduate, a non−CJC ABM graduate or a non−CJC non−ABM graduate will be admitted after taking the entrance exam and interview. The interview will be conducted by the program head;
 
c.	Only graduating students are allowed to take a maximum of thirty (30) units;
d.	The total number of units and the subjects a student may register in a semester shall be in accordance with what is stipulated in the curricular program the student is enrolled in;
e.	Any student may be allowed to carry an overload of not more than 6 units provided, that such are back subjects;
f.	The arrangement of subjects in the curriculum of the course must be strictly followed. A student (1st year to 3rd year) who is enrolled in a subject without passing its prerequisite shall not be given academic credit;
g.	A graduating student may enroll in two subjects simultaneously, one of which is a prerequisite to the other, provided he/she does not exceed the maximum of 30 units as certified by his/her program head;
h.	A student should not have failed 2 times in the same subject. The total number of failed subjects should not be more than 3 subjects per semester; and
i.	A warning will be issued by the program head to a student who failed to comply with the above provision and will be advised to take tutorial classes. A student issued with 3 warnings will be redirected to other programs.
2.2.4.	Bachelor of Science in Business Administration (BSBA)
a.	An ABM CJC graduate will be automatically admitted to the BSBA program after taking the entrance exam;
b.	A non−ABM CJC graduate, a non−CJC ABM graduate or a non−CJC non−ABM graduate will be admitted after taking the entrance exam and interview. The interview will be conducted by the program head;
c.	Only graduating students are allowed to take a maximum of thirty (30) units;
d.	The total number of units and the subjects a student may register in a semester shall be in accordance with what is stipulated in the curricular program the student is enrolled in;
 
e.	Any student may be allowed to carry an overload of not more than 6 units provided, that such are back subjects;
f.	The arrangement of subjects in the curriculum of the course must be strictly followed. A student (1st year to 3rd year) who is enrolled in a subject without passing its prerequisite shall not be given academic credit;
g.	A graduating student may enroll in two subjects simultaneously, one of which is a prerequisite to the other, provided he/she does not exceed the maximum of 30 units as certified by his/her program head;
h.	A student should not have failed 2 times in the same subject. The total number of failed subjects should not be more than 3 subjects per semester; and
i.	A warning will be issued by the program head to a student who failed to comply with the above provision and will be advised to take tutorial classes. A student issued with 3 warnings will be redirected to other programs.
2.2.5.	Bachelor of Science in Hospitality Management (BSHM)
a.	An ABM CJC graduate under Associate Hotel and Restaurant Management will be automatically admitted to the BSHM program without need to take the entrance exam;
b.	An ABM CJC graduate other than Associate Hotel and Restaurant Management, a non−ABM CJC graduate, a non−CJC ABM graduate will be admitted after taking the entrance exam;
c.	A student who fails in any major subject which is a pre− requisite of a higher subject will not be allowed to take higher subjects until he/she passes the said pre− requisite subject;
d.	A student must complete his/her major subjects, except research, to avail the national/international cruise ship familiarization and training;
e.	A student who only passed the research defense can have his/her internship program;
f.	A student must render at least 5 hours duty every semester for institutional gatherings, and duty hours
 
will be deducted from his/her required practicum hours;
g.	Only graduating students are allowed to take a maximum of thirty (30) units; and
h.	The student must be able to obtain at least 3 National Certificates (NC) as a requirement before he/she can graduate in the BSHM programs.

However, student who are in the STEM STRAND and with a distinction of at least HIGH HONORS or a grade of at least 92 in both Manth and Science subjects may opt not to participate.

2.3.2	Transferees
A student may be qualified to proceed to his/her course under the Engineering Program of the College of Engineering if he/she has attained a grade of at least 2.5 or 80% in all his major subjects taken
 
from other schools. This will be a similar requirement for cross− enrolment to other schools although students are strongly advised to take all the major subjects in Cor Jesu College.
Proviso. A student who has a grade of less than 2.5 or 80% in his/her major subject(s) taken from other schools may be allowed to proceed to his/her program in the College of Engineering in this institution provided that he/she shall pass the qualifying examinations for those subject(s) otherwise he/she must retake and pass the said subject(s).

2.3.3	Regular Students. A regular student who fails in any of his/her major subject(s) may be given no more than two (2) chances to retake and pass the subject(s), otherwise he/she shall be redirected to any non−board engineering program.
2.3.4	Students on Probation. A student on probation who fails in any of his/her major subject(s) is no longer given a chance to retake and pass the subject(s) and shall be redirected. to any non−board engineering program.

other program

Proviso. Astudent on probation mayreturn orre−apply in their previous program if they achieve a grade of at least 2.5 in their major subject(s) for the current semester.
2.3.5	Deloading. A student who fails in any of his/her major subject(s) is required to reduce his/her academic load in the succeeding semester. The Program Head or the College Dean determines the number of units to be reduced upon consultation with the concerned professors
2.3.6	Overloading. Only those students who are graduating in
 
that semester are allowed to take an overload of not more than 6 units for as long as his/her total load shall not exceed 30 units whichever is lower.
2.3.7	Passing Score and Cut-off Grade.

Except for the Correlation Subjects, the passing score in all examinations shall be 60% with an equivalent grade of 3.0 or 75%.

The passing score for Correlation Subjects is 75% with an equivalent grade of 3.0. A score of 60% is conditional and will merit one examination retake to pass the subject.
A passing grade of 3.0 will be the basis for entrance to the next level following the pre−requisites of subjects.

2.4.2.	Regular Students
A regular student who fails in any of his/her major subject/s may be given no more than two chances to retake and pass the said subject/s, otherwise he/she shall
 
be redirected.
2.4.3.	Students on Probation
A student on probation who fails in any of his/her major subject/s is no longer given a chance to retake and pass the subject/s and shall now be redirected.
Proviso. A student in probation who fails in his/her major subject/s may be given only one last chance to retake and pass the subject/s if he/she has obtained a general average rating of 2.5 in all of his/her other subjects enrolled during that semester.

2.4.4.	Deloading
A student who fails in any of his/her major subject/s is required to reduce his/her academic load in the succeeding semester. The Program Head, or Dean of College, determines the number of units to be reduced upon consultation with the concerned instructors.
2.4.5.	Overloading
Only those who are graduating in that semester are allowed to take an overload of not more than six (6) units, for as long as his/her total load shall not exceed 30 units.

2.4.6.	Transferees and Cross-Enrollments
A student, from other school, may be qualified to proceed to his/her course under the Computer Studies Programs if he/she has attained a grade of at least 2.5 or 80% in all of his/her major subjects taken from the origin school. The same requirement is set for cross−enrollment to other schools although students are strongly advised to take all of the major subjects in Cor Jesu College.
Proviso. A transferee student who has a grade of less than
2.5 or 80% in his/her major subject/s taken from the origin school may be allowed to proceed to his/her course in the Computer Studies Programs of Cor Jesu College if he/she shall pass the special examination given corresponding to said subject/s, otherwise he/she shall retake and pass the subject/s, accordingly.

2.4.8.	Regular Status
a.	A student who fails in two (2) major subjects will be advised to take a lesser load in the next semester;
b.	If the student fails in three (3) major subjects he/she will be redirected to another field of concentration; and
c.	The basis for cut−off computation of grade is 50% in both minor and major examinations.
2.4.9.	Students on Probation
A student on probation who fails in any of his/her major subject/s is no longer given a chance to retake and pass the subject/s and shall now be redirected.
Proviso. A student in probation who fails in his/her major subject/s may be given only one last chance to retake and pass the subject/s if he/she has obtained a general average rating of 2.5 in all of his/her other subjects enrolled during that semester.

determines the number of units to be reduced upon consultation with the concerned instructors.

The same requirement is set for cross−enrollment to other schools although students are strongly advised to take all of the major subjects in Cor Jesu College.

2.5 or 80% in his/her major subject/s taken from the origin school may be allowed to proceed to his/her course in the College of Engineering and Technology of Cor Jesu College if he/she shall pass the special examination given corresponding to said subject/s, otherwise he/she shall retake and pass the subject/s, accordingly.


2.5.	COLLEGE OF HEALTH SCIENCES (CHS)

2.5.1.	Bachelor of Science in Nursing Program (BSN)
a.	A nursing student must get a general weighted average (WGA) of 82% and must have no grade below 80% in all subjects as well as in the Related Learning Experience (RLE) for him/ her to be retained in the program;
b.	A nursing student must not lack subjects of more than six (6) units of the regular unit load for a semester for him/ her to be promoted to the next level;
c.	A student who fails 50% or more of a semester unit load will be dropped from the program or advised to shift to another program.
 
d.	A student who fails a nursing major subject which constitute 50% or more of the total load is not a criterion for being dropped from the program provided that the student has not failed on other minor subjects;
e.	A student who fails in any nursing subjects shall not be allowed to enroll a nursing major in the next level or semester.
f.	A student is allowed to take or repeat nursing subjects twice only;
g.	To fail twice on the same subjects is a ground for dismissal from the program.
h.	A student dismissed from the program may be considered for readmission by shifting to a different program, provided shifting requisites are met;
i.	A student will undergo counseling after the first failure in any subject with the College Dean and will be referred to the Guidance Counselor;
j.	A student who fails up to 49% of the total academic load should be placed under academic probation. The student will only be allowed to enroll maximum of 18 units the following semester. Moreover, Probation Notice shall be furnished and will be signed by the student and his/her parents/guardians;
k.	A student nurse who gets pregnant while taking the program will be asked to submit obstetrics clearance;
l.	A transferee who failed a major subject in nursing from a previous school and who has been granted admission to the College of Health Sciences, Cor Jesu College, Inc. shall be given only one chance to pass the subject. He/ she would be dropped from the program should the student fail the same subjects.
m.	A nursing student is allowed a maximum of six (6) years residence in the entire program. The program head will inform the College Dean who in turn call the attention of the student the year preceding the expiration of the residency period;
n.	A student who drops a subject before preliminary examination is marked Dropped. However, if she/ he is dropped after preliminary examination he/ she will be marked failed (5.0).
 
o.	A student is encouraged to carry the normal semester load as listed in the curriculum;
p.	A student is encouraged to participate in extracurricular activities provided that these activities will not interfere with his/ her academic studies; and
q.	A student is encouraged to observe pre−requisite subject.
2.5.2.	Bachelor of Science in Midwifery Program (BSM)
a.	A midwifery student must get a general weighted average (WGA) of 80% and must have no grade below 75% in all subjects as well as in the Related Learning Experience (RLE) for him/ her to be retained in the program;
b.	A midwifery student must not lack subjects of more than six (6) units of the regular unit load for a semester for him/ her to be promoted to the next level;
c.	A student who fails 50% or more of a semester unit load is advised to shift to another program;
d.	A student who fails in any Midwifery subject shall not be allowed to take a midwifery major subject in the next level or semester;
e.	A student is allowed to take or repeat Midwifery subjects twice only;
f.	To fail twice on the same subjects is a ground for dismissal from the program;
g.	A student dismissed from the program may be considered for readmission by shifting to different program, provided shifting requisites are met;
h.	A student will undergo counseling after the first failure in any subject with the College Dean and will be referred to the Guidance Counselor;
i.	A student who fails up to 49% of the total academic load should be placed under academic probation. The student will only be allowed to enroll maximum of 18 units the following semester. Moreover, Probation Notice shall be furnished and will be signed by the student and his/her parents/guardians;
j.	A student nurse who gets pregnant while taking the program will be asked to submit obstetrics clearance;
 
k.	A student who drops a subject before Preliminary examination is marked Dropped. However, if she/ he dropped after preliminary examination he/ she will be marked failed (5.0);
l.	A student is encouraged to carry the normal semester load as listed in the curriculum;
r.	A student Midwife is allowed a maximum of six (6) years residence in the entire program. The program head will inform the College Dean who in turn call the attention of the student the year preceding the expiration of the residency period;
m.	A student is encouraged to participate in extracurricular activities provided that these activities will not interfere with his/ her academic studies; and
n.	A student is encouraged to observe pre−requisite subjects.

3.	Policy on Graduates Taking Board Examination
The agreement between the two parties should emphasize that:

3.1.	Any graduating student must seriously and diligently attend the Skill and Competency Enhancement Course provided by the school. At the end of course, the student should take and pass the final examination of the said course. Only then would the student be allowed to graduate, and eventually, take the board exam;

3.1.1	Passing rate for the Skill and Competency Enhancement Course is 75.0% across all areas;
3.1.2	Student who fails to pass the 75.0% passing rate across all areas but gets at least 60.0% average rate shall be allowed to take removal exam only once. If the student fails again to get at least 75.0%, she or he shall be required to re−enroll the course; and
 
3.1.3	A student who gets a rating above 75% but fails in any of the areas of the final examination shall be allowed to take removal exam on the said area only once. If the student fails again to get at least 75.0% on the said area, he or she shall be required to re−enroll the course.
3.2.	After graduation, the student would be highly encouraged to attend another review provided by any of the review centers with very good track record of passing percentage in any licensure examination. As proof of attendance, the student must present the official attendance sheet provided by the center, duly signed by its authorized signatories;

3.3.	Only after the two preceding conditions shall have been fulfilled by the student would the school allow him/her to take the licensure examination;
3.4.	An incentive scheme would be considered by the school administration to motivate the board takers not just to pass the exam, but also to strive for a much higher board performance;

3.5.	Graduates who will top the PRC Board examination will be given refund on the tuition and miscellaneous of the whole year on the school year last attended:
3.5.1.	Top 1: 100% of the tuition and miscellaneous fees of the last school year attended
3.5.2.	Top 2: 90% of the tuition fees and miscellaneous fees of the last school year attended
3.5.3.	Top 3: 80% of the tuition fees and miscellaneous fees of the last school year attended
3.5.4.	Top 4: 70% of the tuition fees of the last school year attended
3.5.5.	Top 5: 60% of the tuition fees of the last school year attended
3.5.6.	Top 6 to top 10: 50% of the tuition fees of the last school year attended
 
C.	EXAMINATIONS

1.	A student's financial obligation must be fully settled and paid as per assessment schedule before taking the examination. (BOT, Res. No. 008, S. 2008);
2.	Every student must get his/her examination permit from the Finance Office before every examination period;
3.	During the examination, the instructor signs the permit. No permit No exam.
4.	A student caught cheating during the examination will get a failing mark in that particular subject;
5.	Special Examinations are given for excused absences in the Midterm and Final Exams;
6.	Special Examinations are given only within two weeks or ten (10) school days after the examinations.;
7.	A special examination may be arranged by the student with the office of the Dean of College Department. The arrangement must be made at least two days before the first day of the examination schedule;
8.	The following are the steps in taking special examinations:

8.1.	The student applies for a special permit from the Dean of College Department.
8.2.	The student pays his/her special examination fee at the Finance Office.
8.3.	The student presents an official receipt to the Dean of College and	secures a special exam permit.
8.4.	The student presents the Special Examination Permit to the Dean who will set the date and time for special exams for all subjects.
The teacher is under no obligation to grant any exemption. However, a college policy of exempting students from final examinations is implemented under the following guidelines:

8.4.1.	The student has kept a grade of at least 1.5 for the semester
8.4.2.	He/she has not incurred more than three (3) unexcused absences.
8.4.3.	He/she has not been guilty of outright unbecoming behavior.
8.4.4.	Exemption is official when approved and posted by the Dean of the College.

1.	Higher Education
1.1.	The Higher Education, except the College of Health Sciences, adopts the numerical grading system, with the following grades points:

1.0 = 95 – 100

1.7	=88	2.7	=78

2.0	=85	3.0	=75
5.0 – FAILED
6.0 – WITHDRAWN
7.0 – DROPPED
8.0 − INCOMPLETE
2.4 – NO TEST

1.2.	An incomplete grade must be completed within 30 days following the giving of an INCOMPLETE (8.0), otherwise it becomes a 5.0 or a failure;

1.6.	For a student to get a passing mark, he/she has to get at least 60% of a given quiz and examination;
1.7.	Report cards are given to the students twice during the semester, after the Midterm and Final Examinations;
1.8.	Report cards are mailed to the parents after the Final Examinations; and
1.9.	If a student would like some explanations regarding the grade he/she received for a certain subject, he/she may consult the instructor of the subject.

2.	College of Health Sciences Grading System

2.1.	Grade Computation for the Subject with RLE
Prelim Grade	= 2/3 class standing + 1/3 Prelim Exam
= 60% PG Theory + 40% PG RLE
Midterm Grade	= 2/3 class standing + 1/3 Midterm Exam
= 60% MTG Theory + 40% MTG RLE
Pre−Final Grade	= 2/3 class standing + 1/3 Pre−final Exam
= 60% PFG Theory + 40% Pre−Final RLE
 
Temp. Final Grade  = 2/3 class standing + 1/3 Final Exam
= 60% TFG Theory + 40% TFG RLE
Final Grade = (((PG + MG + PFG + TFG) /4) x70%) + 30% Compre
2.2.	Grade Computations for subjects having no RLE

Prelim Grade	= 2/3 Class standing + 1/3 Prelim Exam Midterm Grade	= 2/3 Class standing + 1/3 Midterm Exam Pre−Final Grade	= 2/3 Class standing + 1/3 Pre−Final Exam Temp−Final = 2/3 Class standing + 1/3 Temp. Final Exam
Final Grade = (((PG + MG + PFG + TFG) /4) x70% )+ 30% Compre

Comprehensive Exam	= (RS/TS) x 60 + 40
2.1.	A student who fails to take a quiz / long examination gets a zero score. No Incomplete grade is given;
2.2.	Cut−off Mark
The College uses a 60−40 cut−off mark. For a student to get a passing mark, he/she has to get at least 60% of a given quiz or examination.

% Equivalent = Raw Score
Total Items

E.	Graduation Requirements
1.	Graduating students must file their application for graduation on the date set by the Registrar's Office. Late applicants will be fined and may even be advised to postpone their graduation;
2.	The above−mentioned application must be recommended by the Program Head to be approved by the Dean of College and endorsed to the Registrar for final approval;
3.	A graduating student is required to attend the retreat for graduating students;
4.	A graduating student is also required to attend to the practices and other activities of graduating students. Failure of compliance without valid reason and approval from the Director of Student Services is a ground for disqualification of the student to participate in the commencement exercises; and
5.	Students will be allowed to participate in the Commencement Exercises only if they have satisfactorily completed all academic
 
requirements prescribed by the institution and the Commission on Higher Education and have fully paid their financial obligation to the school. (BOT, Res.008, s. 2008).

(Candidate for Latin Honors marked Dropped, No Test and Incomplete is automatically disqualified.)
G.	Annual Academic Awards
1.	Awards for academic excellence may be given by the College to the graduating and under−graduate students at the end of the school year;
2.	All the academic units, at least 36 units in all baccalaureate programs, except in the last academic year of Education program which requires 30 units, must have been earned at Cor Jesu College during that academic year;
3.	Driving, PE and NSTP grades must not be less than 2.5;
4.	The Gold Medalist must have a general weighted average of 1.2 with no semestral grade lower than 1.5;
5.	The Silver Medalist must have a general weighted average of 1.4 with no semestral grade lower than 1.7; and
 
6.	The Bronze Medalist must have a general weighted average of 1.6 with no semestral grade lower than 1.9.

A.	ENROLMENT PROCESS

ONLINE ENROLMENT PROCESS

STEP 1.	SIGNIFY INTENT TO ENROLL
Point your browser to OLSEN
at https://apps.cjc.edu.ph/guide−to−olsen online− student.../ . Take note of the guidelines before proceeding to the online form.

STEP 2.		FILL OUT ELECTRONIC FORM IN OLSEN (ONLINE STUDENT ENROLLMENT) SYSTEM
Fulfill all electronic requirements together with OLSEN entry. Communicate with your respective program personnel online (chat) for such requirements and where to submit soft copies.
STEP 3.	SECURE CLEARANCE TO PROCEED
In the OLSEN web page, go to “Check My Enrollment Status” menu (Green Box) to check status of enrollment. Be ready with your Enrollment Reference Number and birth date for validation.

STEP 4.	PAY ENTRANCE FEE
Pay entrance fee at any of the official payment channels. (See https://apps.cjc.edu.ph/payment−channels/ for a list of payment channels)
Be sure to follow up with Finance Office through Messenger (m.me/cjcfinanceoffice).

STEP 5.	FILL UP GUIDANCE CENTER QUESTIONNAIRE
Follow the link to the Google Form
https://sites.google.com/g.cjc.edu.ph/cjcguidance/guidance
−questionnaire
STEP 6.	SUBJECT PICKING/CLASS SCHEDULES
Coordinate with your respective program head for the list of subjects needed for the semester.
 
STEP 7.	SUBMIT ENROLMENT FORM FOR FINAL CHECKING
Proceed to the Registrar and submit enrolment form for final checking and

STEP 8.	SECURE ASSESSMENT FORM
Proceed to Assessment Section and receive assessment form

WALK-IN OR FACE TO FACE ENROLMENT PROCESS

STEP 1.	SIGNIFY INTENT TO ENROLL
Proceed to Student Services Center to secure enrolment form.

STEP 2.	FILL OUT ELECTRONIC FORM IN OLSEN (ONLINE STUDENT ENROLLMENT) SYSTEM
Proceed to ICT section and ask assistance for OLSEN entry or open https://apps.cjc.edu.ph/guide−to−olsenonline− student.../  then follow procedures. Take note of the
guidelines before proceeding to the online form.

STEP 3.	SECURE CLEARANCE TO PROCEED
(For new students and transferees, proceed to the school clinic then Go back to Student Services Center for the clearance to proceed.
STEP 4.	PAY ENTRANCE FEE
Proceed to the Cashier to pay.

STEP 5.	FILL UP GUIDANCE CENTER QUESTIONNAIRE
Proceed to Guidance Center to fill up questionnaire or Follow the link to the Google Form
https://sites.google.com/g.cjc.edu.ph/cjcguidance/guidance
−questionnaire
STEP 6.	SUBJECT PICKING/CLASS SCHEDULES
Proceed to your respective College to enroll subjects for the semester.
 
STEP 7.	SUBMIT ENROLMENT FORM FOR FINAL CHECKING
Proceed to the Registrar and submit enrolment form for final checking and

STEP 8.	SECURE ASSESSMENT FORM
Proceed to Assessment Section and receive assessment form

B.	ENROLMENT POLICIES

1.	Students who have incomplete requirements are asked to apply for temporary admission from the Student Services Center approved by the School Registrar;
2.	Students who request for cross−enrolment to another school must seek the endorsement of the Dean of the College in concurrence with the Program Head and the approval from the School Registrar;
3.	Students who decide to change program or major need a permit endorsed by the Dean of College and approved by the School Registrar;
4.	Students who request for overloads need the endorsement of the Program Head and the approval of the Dean of the College the School Registrar;
5.	The school requires all students to fully pay their back accounts before they are re−admitted to the school. In case the parent cannot fully settle his son's/daughter's accounts, the students may be temporarily enrolled. However, the parent is required to fill−out a temporary admission form and a promissory note. When the back accounts are not settled as promised, the student will be automatically dropped from the enrolment list; and
6.	The school reserves the right to refuse enrolment of students who have records of misconduct on or off campus.
C.	POLICY ON GENERAL ADMISSION AND RE-ADMISSION OF STUDENTS

1.	Cor Jesu College adopts the policy on open admission but selective retention.
2.	The College admits eligible student to any Higher Education and ITVET Programs if he/she has any of the following:
 
2.1.	He/She has academic deficiencies resulting to their disqualification to the required academic standard of the program they wish to graduate;
2.1.	He/She has major violation of school rules and regulations pursuant to the implementation of College Student Handbook Section 7, Article 1.1 on major offenses to wit: Category A. Expulsion and Category B. Exclusion;
2.1.	His/Her continued enrollment is prejudicial to his/her own health or to the health of others in the College; and
2.1.	He/She has failed to meet his/her financial obligation to the College.
3.	The College denies re−admission of students to any collegiate and vocational technology programs if he/she has any of the following:

3.1.	He/She has academic deficiencies resulting to their disqualification to the required academic standard of the program they wish to graduate;
D.	WITHDRAWAL OF CREDENTIALS AND ENROLMENT

1.	An applicant should secure a notice of withdrawal form from the Office of the Registrar and seek the signature of heads listed on the form;
2.	Credentials submitted by transferees and freshmen will only be returned if all the financial obligations, as assessed by the Finance Office, shall have been settled;
3.	For students under a penalty of suspension or expulsion, credentials shall only be released until after the lifting of the penalty;
4.	A student who transfers and withdraws, within two weeks after the beginning of classes and who has already paid the pertinent tuition and other school fees in full or for any length longer than one month may be charged ten percent of the total amount due for the term if he/she withdraws within the first week of classes, or twenty percent if within the second week of classes, regardless of whether or not he/she has actually attended the classes. The student may be charged all the school fees in full if he/she withdraws any time after the second week of classes. However, if the transfer or withdrawal is due to a justifiable reason, the student shall be charged the pertinent fees only up to and including the last month of attendance; and
5.	A student who transfers and withdraws his/her credentials must turn over their school I.D at the Student Services Center.
 
E.	ISSUANCE OF SCHOOL CREDENTIALS

1.	Certificate of Transfer Credentials (Honorable Dismissal). An applicant should file a request for a Certificate of Transfer Credentials (CTC) at the Office of the School Registrar. The Credential will be released subject to clearance from the different offices listed in the request form.
2.	Diploma and Special Orders (S.O.). An applicant should secure clearance slip from the Finance Office with the signature of the yearbook coordinator before Diploma can be released; and Diploma shall be issued only once.
3.	Transcript of Records (TOR). An applicant should secure clearance for the release of TOR.
4.	Issuance of Credentials to a Proxy. The proxy must present his/her I.D. and a copy of a Special Power of Attorney (SPA) allowing him/her to secure the documents before the documents will be released.
5.	Withholding of Credentials. The administration reserves the right to withhold the release of credentials of students, who are under investigation or administrative sanctions.
 
SECTION IV.
Class Attendance and Absences

A.	GENERAL RULES ON ATTENDANCE AND ABSENCES

1.	Regular attendance and punctuality in every subject enrolled are required of each student;
2.	Attendance is counted from the first day of regular classes;
3.	Late enrollees are admitted only within two weeks from the start of classes, provided that they will pay the corresponding fee specified;
4.	Since tardiness is not tolerated in class, students are considered absent if they are not present within the first 15 minutes of the class period. Three instances of being late, each not exceeding 15 minutes should be counted as an unexcused absence;
5.	A student who asks permission to leave his/her class after the roll call but does not return within 10 minutes from the time he/she is given permission, shall be considered absent;
6.	An absence from class whether personal or official is recorded as one absence but still subject to classification of absences;
7.	Scheduled recollections and/or retreats are considered as class hours;
8.	Attendance in non−classroom activities shall be correspondingly credited to class attendance on the day the activity is held (field trips, seminars, workshops, symposia; official sports tournaments; and other official contests, etc.) as long as the activity has approval from the school authorities, and considered official;
9.	A student is held responsible for the lesson assignment and requirement for the entire content of the course, no matter how long or for what reason his/her absence is made; and
10.	A student who has incurred absences of more than 20% of the total class hours in a given time should not be given credit for the program or subject (Article XIV, Section 73 of the Revised Manual of Regulations for Private Schools)
 
B.	MAXIMUM NUMBER OF ABSENCES ALLOWED
1. 1−unit subject	−	3 hours
2. 2−unit subject	−	7 hours
3. 3−unit subject	−	10 hours
4. 5−unit subject	−	18 hours
5. 6−unit subject	−	21 hours
6. 7−unit subject	−	24 hours
7. 8−unit subject	−	27 hours:

C.	EXCUSED ABSENCES
1.	Death of a member of the immediate family (parent, brother/sister, spouse and child);
2.	Hospitalization/illness;
3.	Doctor's order;
4.	SK members attending sessions/seminars;
5.	Attendance in seminars, retreats and recollections; and
6.	Attendance in meetings and other official representations of the college such as competitions, conferences and the like.

D.	PROCEDURES OF THE ISSUANCE OF SLIPS
1.	Excused Absence Slip. The student is required to get an excused absence slip at least within three school days after the last day of his/her absence. The student presents a medical certificate (if hospitalized) and/or an excuse letter in case of seminars, competitions, conferences, and other school official representations to the Prefect of Student Formation as a requirement for the issuance of excused absence slip.

2.	Last Chance Slip (Pink). The student presents himself/herself to the Guidance Counselor and secures a counseling slip to be given to the Prefect of Student Formation as a requirement for the issuance of last chance slip. A student is required to secure pink slip immediately after he/she is declared dropped. If a student makes another absence, he/she is dropped for good regardless of any reasons. Instructors are advised not to admit said students in their respective class/classes anymore.
 
SECTION V.
Scholarships
A.	ACADEMIC SCHOLARSHIPS

1.	Classification of Scholarships
1.1.	Full-Scholarship
1.1.1.	Senior High School Graduate with Highest Distinction provided that the school where he/she came from has 50 or more graduates;
1.1.2.	Those who obtained 85 and above percentile rank in the Cor Jesu College Freshmen Scholarship Examination;
1.1.3.	Dean's Listers with weighted average of not less than 1.34999 and with no grade lower than 1.5; and
1.1.4.	Those who won as champions in the Cor Jesu College Battle of the Academic Wizard.
1.2.	Half-Scholarship
1.2.1.	Senior High School Graduate with High Distinction provided that the school where he/she came from has 50 or more number graduates;
1.2.2.	Those who obtained 76−84 percentile rank in the Cor Jesu College Freshmen Scholarship Examination;
1.2.3.	Dean's Listers with weighted average of not less than 1.44999 with no grade lower than 1.7; and
1.2.4.	Those who won as 1st runners−ups in the Cor Jesu College Battle of the Academic Wizard

1.3.	One-Fourth-Scholarship
1.3.1.	Those who obtained 60−75 percentile rank in the Cor Jesu College Freshmen Scholarship Examination;
1.3.2.	Those who won as 2nd runners−up in the Cor Jesu College Battle of the Academic Wizard; and
1.3.3.	Those who were high school first to fifth honorable mentions.
 
2.	Requirements and Procedures for Academic Scholarships

3.	Policies on Academic Scholarship

3.1.	All academic scholarship grants are good for only one semester. Grades have to be maintained in order to be included in the Dean's List;
3.2.	The High School Valedictorian/Top 1 and Salutatorian/Top 2 should come from the graduating class with no less than 50 students in order to qualify for academic scholarship;
3.3.	The scholarship grants of the respective winners of CJC Battle of the Academic Wizard can be enjoyed by the alternate in case one of them is not desirous to study at CJC; and
3.4.	The Dean's List scholars having either full, half or one fourth tuition fee grants shall have at least 18 units as academic loads which shall include Religious Studies, Driving, Physical Education and NSTP. These are qualifying subjects in which the scholars should achieve a final grade of not less than 2.5.
3.5.	The ratio for the number of academic scholars shall be 1:100 or one (1) academic scholar for every 100−student population.
