2.	Privileges and Conditions

3.	Policies on Non-Academic Scholarship

3.1.	Non−academic scholar can enjoy one scholarship at a time by choosing whichever has higher privileges.
3.2.	A student can be member of the TerpsiCorean Performing Group or the Red Ambassador Band even without incentives;
3.3.	The school will refund a CJC scholar with outside scholarship.
3.4.	A scholar who has an approved load below the prescribed units given them cannot enjoy refund from the school. However, they can use them for paying other school fees;
3.5.	A scholar who failed in his/her subject/s of the previous semester and was accepted for a valid reason in the succeeding semester is required to pay for the failed subject/s when he/she will re−enroll it;
3.6.	A non−academic scholar who is found guilty of grave offense on and off campus will be removed from the list of scholars;
3.7.	All student assistants are prohibited to engage in any fraternity and sorority that practices hazing. A student assistant who will be
 
caught violating this policy will be dismissed from the scholarship after due process has been conducted; and
3.8.	A Non−Academic Scholarship is only for one semester and renewable thereafter
3.9.	A non−Academic Scholarship is limited to the curriculum year of the program to which the student−scholar is enrolled.
4.	Subject Loads, Grades, Duties, and Responsibilities

4.1.	Student Assistants
4.1.1.	An apprentice must have a minimum of 18−unit load during the regular semester and a maximum of 6−unit load during summer;
4.1.2.	A regular SA must have a minimum of 18 and maximum of 22−unit load every semester and maximum of 6 during summer;
4.1.3.	An apprentice and regular SA must work at least 4 hours every school day regardless of subject loads;
4.1.4.	Assignment to or transfer from one office to another requires approval from the Office of the Human Resource Department; and
4.1.5.	Incomplete grades must be completed before the start of the succeeding semester.
4.2.	Band Members, Dance Troupe and Athletic Scholars
4.2.1.	They must have a minimum of 12 and a maximum of 22− unit load. Otherwise, the scholar needs the approval from the Director for Student Services;
4.2.2.	They must have no incomplete grades before the start of the preceding semester; and
4.2.3.	They must be available for practices and official performances.

4.3.	Fr. Andre Coindre and other non-academic school scholars
4.3.1.	They must have a maximum of 22−unit load every semester; and
4.3.2.	They must have no incomplete and failing grades before the succeeding semester.
 
5.	Evaluation and Termination of Non-Academic Scholars

5.1.	Non−academic scholars are evaluated according to the criteria set by the school before the end of each semester by the moderators or coaches or heads of office;
5.2.	A non−academic scholar who wants to stop during the semester, especially in the case of SA, must give an official notice one month before officially resigning; and
5.3.	A non−academic scholar who is convicted of violating any school policy on and off campus will be removed from the list of scholars.

6.	Requirements for Renewal of Scholarship

6.1.	Evaluation of the office heads or moderators or coaches;
6.2.	Grades in all the subjects taken from the previous semester; and
6.3.	Submission of filled−out application form to the Student Servicer Center and/or Human Resource Office.
 
SECTION VI.
Institutional Rules and Norms
A.	RIGHTS AND FREEDOM OF STUDENTS
The rights and freedom of students are to be exercised with responsibility and prudence. The students should not use them to discredit their fellow students, the College and its school personnel, or to prevent them from performing the roles and functions required of them. Any violation thereof is a ground for investigation and sanctions as specified in this College Student Handbook. Cor Jesu College recognizes these rights and freedom:
1.	The privilege to be admitted and retained in the College is subject to the specific provisions stipulated in this College Student Handbook and those that may be promulgated by the institution;
2.	The student has the right to be protected from disclosure of personal data, academic grades, counseling, disciplinary and other school records to anybody without his or her approval;
3.	He/She has the right to be protected against improper academic evaluation and to know their evaluation or grades right after the deadline for submission of grades set by the College Dean. A student may appeal for a grade he/she thinks was unfairly and mistakenly given by the teacher;
4.	He/she has the right to be protected against unprofessional and unethical conduct of school personnel like the following:

4.1.	Consistent failure of the teacher to meet his/her class without reasonable explanation;
4.2.	Discriminatory or prejudicial actions of the teacher against the student/s inside the classroom;
4.3.	Consistent failure of the teacher to present learning materials relevant to the course, and consistent failure of the teacher to present test results and grades;
4.4.	All immoral acts like sexual harassment, oral defamation and the like, committed by the school personnel to the student/s; and
4.5.	He/she has the right to participate in the review or formulation of rules or policies that directly affect their welfare. The College Student Government President is the official representative of the students in the following:
 
4.5.1.	Coordinating Council for College Affairs (COCOCOA);
4.5.2.	Students Services Council;
4.5.3.	Student Disciplinary Board; and
4.5.4.	Student Financial Assistance
5.	He/she has the right to enjoy freedom of expression, membership of organizations and clubs and in the election of class and CSG officers and associations, provided that the requirements specified by the school are complied with; and
6.	No student shall be subjected to disciplinary action, like suspension, exclusion and expulsion without due process as stipulated in this handbook and explained in the Manual of Regulations for Private Schools.
B.	PROPER CONDUCT AND BEHAVIOR

1.	Conduct inside the school
As a Catholic Educational Institution, the school trains and forms students to be responsible citizens of the community and the country as a whole. Thus, good manners and right conduct must be observed by the students at all times in dealing with visitors, school personnel and co− students. Any infraction of the school rules and policies by the students is subject to investigation by the school personnel and must be given corresponding interventions upon the recommendation of the school authorities. The following are expected of a CJC student:
1.1.	He/she	must	not	utter	offensive,	vulgar,	indecent	or blasphemous words;
1.2.	He/she is not allowed to whistle, howl or make abusive or offensive remarks at anybody;
1.3.	He/she is prohibited from bringing pornographic pictures and materials inside the campus;
1.4.	The areas exclusively for ladies are off−limits to men. At no instance should male students intrude upon the privacy of the ladies in these places. Likewise, this is also true for areas exclusively for men;
1.5.	In areas like classrooms, corridors, library, laboratories, piazza and areas near the classrooms, students are prohibited to make unnecessary noise such as whistling, boisterous conversations, loud talking, laughing, singing and other forms of disturbances when classes or examinations are going on;
 
1.6.	Students are prohibited in staying in classrooms and laboratories after the last period in the evening classes unless given permission by the school authorities for their use;
1.7.	Students are prohibited from staying in dark places, inside parked vehicles and in unlighted rooms or corners;
1.8.	Students are prohibited from scandalous display of amorous behavior
1.9.	Students must refrain from depiction or portrayal of licentiousness or lewdness on stage or within the school campus;
1.10.	Students are expected to take extra care in using school property. Thus, they must not perform any acts that will cause harm or destruction to the school property;
1.11.	Students must properly return all borrowed furniture like chairs, tables and others to their respective places after use;
1.12.	Students must secure permission from the Student Services Center for the use of the public address system;
1.13.	Students are expected to take good care of the school surroundings. Thus, they must avoid littering in the campus. They are requested to follow the “Clean−as You−Go” (CLAY−GO) program of the school. They are encouraged to segregate and throw their garbage properly;
1.14.	Students are prohibited from smoking and drinking liquor at all times inside the school campus. They are also prohibited from smoking in at least 100 meters from the campus. (CMO No. 63, S. 2007);
1.15.	Students are not allowed to indulge in any form of gambling inside the campus.
1.16.	Students are prohibited to join in any fraternities, sororities and any groups or associations that practice hazing as these are detrimental to their well−being;
1.17.	Students are formed to be prayerful. Thus, they are required to join masses, prayer meetings, retreats and recollections. They are also required to pray the Angelus which is part of the tradition of Cor Jesu College. They should remain still when they hear the prayer. The non−Catholics are expected to stay put and remain silent; and
1.18.	Students who invite guests from outside the campus as lecturers, speakers of seminar, are required to submit a letter to the Director for Student Services for the approval of the activity. The letter should contain the names of persons involved, the purposes of their activity and expected time of arrival and
 
departure of the guests. If they are VIPs' or high−ranking public officials, the organizing group must coordinate with the Special Assistant on Security Matters for safety and security of the visitor(s).
C.	CLASSROOM DISCIPLINE

1.	Students should be prompt in attending their classes by going to their respective classrooms on the first bell. If the instructor is late for 15 minutes after the second bell, the class is considered dismissed. In cases where the instructor sends a word for the class to wait, then the students must wait;
2.	The students are not allowed to crowd at the entrance and places adjacent of each classroom before the first bell;
3.	Students should do transactions (other than academics) with fellow students during the break, and not during class hours;
4.	Students shall bring with them pens and pieces of paper, calculators and other needed classroom materials;
5.	Students are prohibited from eating inside the classroom, library and laboratories, unless given permission by the school authorities or as part of the classroom processes or demonstrations;
6.	Any student who wishes to address a class or make an announcement must secure a written note containing the recommendations of the DSS and the approval of the Dean of College. This must be shown to the instructor before addressing the class;
7.	Students are expected to respond only when acknowledged by the teacher.
8.	Students who do not cooperate with ordinary classroom procedures and those who show disrespectful conduct, may be sent to the Prefect of Student Formation. A student who is sent out from class must hand−carry a written note from the Prefect of Student Formation authorizing him/her to enter the class at the next meeting;
9.	Students who do not wear any of the following: Prescribed uniform, ribbon, CJC pin, I.D., cord, shoes are not allowed to enter the classroom unless they have an approved uniform dispensation slip from the Prefect of Student Formation or the Director for Student Services;
10.	Students must practice honesty by heart. Any student caught cheating shall be given zero in a particular test without prejudice of being investigated by the Prefect of Student Formation and given
 
commensurate intervention if and when found responsible for doing such action;
11.	Writing or carving on chairs, tables, walls and destroying them in whatever ways are forms of vandalism, which are prohibited. Any student caught will be investigated;
12.	Students should switch off their mobile phones/mobile multimedia players in the classroom, library and laboratories. Laptop, notebooks, cellular phones and the like may be permitted when use for instructional purposes;
13.	Students are prohibited from putting their feet on chairs, tables and walls, and sitting on the arms of chairs;
14.	Students are allowed to use the chalkboard/whiteboard for educational purposes only;
15.	The students are asked to switch off the ceiling fans and lights in the classrooms when they are not being used; and
16.	All Students are not allowed to take the final examination without an examination permit. In the absence of an examination permit, a student must get a promissory note from the Finance Office to be able to take the examination. (“No Permit No Exam Policy”).

D.	CONDUCT OUTSIDE THE SCHOOL CAMPUS

1.	The student who is enrolled in the College has the responsibility of safeguarding the name and upholding the reputation of CJC. The students are expected to have known and integrated the shared beliefs and core values of the school. Therefore, they are expected to behave according to these beliefs and values; and
2.	The student is held responsible for his/ her misconduct and unlawful activities outside the campus. Any complaint of scandalous behavior or misconduct outside the campus will be investigated by the Student Disciplinary Board.

E.	GOOD GROOMING
1.	Gentlemen are required to have a regular haircut prescribed by the school.
2.	Social norms dictate that the use of make−up, lipstick, and the plucking or shaving of eyebrows will only be for ladies unless men are required to use these for educational purposes;
 
3.	Male students are prohibited from wearing earrings or face rings on the school campus and during school−sponsored activities outside the campus;
4.	All Students are not allowed to color their hair with unnatural color for whatever reason unless otherwise they are needed for school special events or other presentation related to school activities. (They are given only one week to recolor their hair to natural color after the activity that they have participated); and
5.	Gentlemen Criminology students are required to have their regular army haircut or white sidewall (4x7).

F.	RULES ON SCHOOL UNIFORM AND ATTIRE DURING NON-UNIFORM DAYS

1.	The standard campus uniforms are as follows:
For the ladies:
1.1.	School prescribed blouse and skirt, crimson red ribbon (v−form) with CJC pin, BLACK SHOES, with school ID. The edge of the skirt should be three inches below the knee; and
1.2.	The crimson red ribbon should measure three inches in length, half inch in width, slanted cut, one inch apart. It is pinned by a school seal between the collars of the blouse.

For the gentlemen:
1.3.	School prescribed white, short−sleeved, loose polo shirt with pocket, and a PLAIN WHITE UNDER SHIRT. These are worn with loose gray slack pants, black shoes, socks, CJC pin and school ID.

2.	Wednesday Attire (uniform−free day)
2.1.	Female students are allowed to wear any decent attire such as full chest, skirt and blouse with sleeves, polo shirt and long pair of pants, worn with the school ID and a pair of shoes or a pair of sandals. See−through clothing, t−shirts, tight mini−skirts, shorts, tattered pants, plunging neckline, sleeveless and hanging skirts/blouses, slippers are prohibited among female students; and
 
2.2.	Male students are allowed to wear any decent attire such as, polo, polo shirt or long sleeves worn with the school ID and a pair of shoes. Sleeveless, t−shirts, hanging shirts, tattered pants, short pants, cross dresses, see−through clothing, sandals, slippers are prohibited among male students.
3.	Saturday and Sunday Attire

3.1.	CSP Students are required to wear school uniform with ID. PE uniform shall only be used during PE classes after which students are asked to change and wear again the school uniform during their other classes;

3.2.	Regular Students entering the campus on Saturdays and Sundays for organizational or class activities and other official activities of the school, are required to wear decent and appropriate attire. Allowed and prohibited attires during Wednesdays hold true during these days. Students are allowed to wear decent t−shirts or their organizational or college/program customized shirts either with or without collars.

This provision holds true as well during other non−uniform days for on−campus or off−campus activities, such as family day, intramural activities, foundation day, recollection, community engagements and other activities and celebrations that do not require wearing of uniform.
4.	Uniform for Other Programs.

4.1.	Uniform of students for BS−HRM, BSN, BS−Criminology and Technical Vocational Education is specified by the school. Please refer to the Dean of the College for details;

4.2.	The school uniform must be worn within the school premises and in all school functions unless otherwise permitted by those in authority;
4.3.	Entrance of a student to the campus shall be denied when he/she is not wearing the complete uniform.  He/she is only allowed
 
entrance when issued a uniform dispensation slip by the Prefect of Student Formation or the Director for Students Services;

4.4.	Non−wearing of school uniform may be allowed for students who are involved in stage presentation and in preparation for extra and co−curricular activities. However, they are required to present a letter to the teacher approved by the Prefect of Student Formation or the Director for Student Services;
4.5.	The student who is working outside the school may be exempted from wearing school uniform but is required to wear his/her office uniform. To get an exemption, he/she is required to submit a certificate of employment to the Prefect of Student Formation to be approved by the Director of Students Services. In the absence of an office uniform, the student is required to wear the school uniform;

4.6.	A pregnant student who is allowed to continue her studies in the school is exempted from wearing school uniform and is required instead to wear maternity dress;

4.7.	Students who are on−the−job training (OJT) and those who are in their practicum years must wear their OJT and Practicum uniform when entering the campus;
4.8.	P.E. students should wear a standard uniform prescribed by the administration. They shall wear their uniform during their class schedules. P.E. uniform will only be worn during P.E. classes;

4.9.	Students are prohibited from wearing t−shirts or any attire with vulgar words or pictures and sketches that portray pornography; and

4.10.	A student who deviates from the prescribed attire is prohibited from entering the campus. Any student who has gained entrance and has not followed the rules will be asked to report to the Prefect of Student Formation or to the Director for Student Services.
 
G.	WEARING OF SCHOOL ID WITH CORD, PIN AND RIBBON FOR WOMEN

1.	The wearing of school ID with CJC cord, school pin, and ribbon which is exclusive for women is mandatory inside the campus on all days except on Wednesdays and weekends when only IDs are required;
2.	The student who does not have the ID because of the late issuance must secure dispensation slip from the Prefect of Student Formation;
3.	The lending and borrowing of ID from another student are prohibited;
4.	The student who loses his/her ID must report immediately to the Student Services Center. The following must be complied with:

7.1.	Submit an affidavit of loss;
7.2.	Fill−out requisition form;
7.3.	Pay at the cashier;
7.4.	Proceed to CIMS for printing; and
7.5.	Proceed to the Student Services Center for issuance of ID validation sticker.
5.	Validation sticker for ID is changed every semester and is given only to enroled students of the College.

H.	SCHOOL PUBLICATIONS

This refers to all printed, mimeographed or photocopied materials published by the school or by the students for on or off−campus circulation. Included are the various materials used to inform the community about the activities on − or off−campus.
1.	Posting and Distribution of Materials
1.1.	Announcement for posting and distribution must have clearance from the Student Services Center and it must be properly signed. Neither initials nor aliases or incomplete name of author of article will be allowed;
1.2.	The College allows posting only of advertisement of materials and commodities related to education and community welfare, school supplies and equipment; and
1.3.	Students' Bulletin board will be used for announcement written on paper or presentable materials.
2.	Ethical Guidelines for Campus Journalism
The College forms young journalists who are guided by the institution's beliefs, core values and by the basic principles of responsible journalism.
 
2.1.	Articles, pictures and illustrations should uphold Christian moral values and promote the Vision, Mission and Core Values of the College;
2.2.	Articles of publications must be accurate, impartial and well− researched;
2.3.	Attacks on the person or any member of the community like students, school and its personnel should be avoided;
2.4.	Complete name of the author must be written or indicated in the article such as opinion or comments he/she has submitted; and
2.5.	The proper choice of themes and the use of decent language, expressed in correct grammar befitting the school must be observed at all times.


3.	Legal Guidelines Based from Republic Act Number 7079

3.1.	The staff of the publication shall be responsible to the school and to the third parties for its decisions, actions, policies and legal consequences arising from such;
3.2.	Tertiary student publications are founded on accepted journalism principles and ethical practices and are regulated by the laws on journalism and press freedom;
3.3.	Editorial policies shall see to it that the news are reported accurately and verified carefully. Reports which are libelous or violating the person's right to privacy or adversely affect private reputation shall be avoided;
3.4.	The school administration shall not be held responsible or accountable for any breach of law or regulation pertaining to press or media matters. The editorial board jointly shall be held responsible for the contents of the student's or school's publication. The editorial board consists of the following:
3.4.1.	Editor−in−Chief
3.4.2.	Associate Editor
3.4.3.	Managing Editor
3.4.4.	Opinion Editor
3.4.5.	News Editor
3.4.6.	Feature Editor
3.4.7.	Sports Editor
 
3.4.8.	Photojournalist
3.4.9.	Cartoonist
3.4.10.	Staff Writers
3.4.11.	Moderator/Technical Adviser
3.5.	Member of the school publication staff must maintain his/her satisfactory academic standing in order to retain membership in the staff;
3.6.	To promote the philosophy, beliefs and values of the College, it only allows school publication to operate in the campus; and
3.7.	In case of grave violations of the law of the press/media, public policy and school rules, and if found responsible for doing such by a competent body, the student concerned shall be subjected to disciplinary action by the College.
I.	RELEASING OF TRANSFER CREDENTIALS PROHIBITION
The release of the transfer credentials of any student may be withheld for reasons of student disciplinary sanctions such suspension, exclusion or expulsion. Non−payment of financial obligations of students to the school is also a ground for withholding student’s transfer credentials. The credentials shall be released as soon as his/her obligation shall have been settled or the penalty of suspension, exclusion or expulsion lifted.

J.	RELEASING OF SCHOOL RECORD OF STUDENTS
1.	A student records such as grades, disciplinary cases documents and other school records or documents are confidential. Therefore, they can only be released upon request of the students’ concerned;
2.	If a student is still a minor, his/her parents or guardians have the right to access his/her school records even without his or her permission; and
3.	If a student is of legal age, his or her student records cannot be revealed or released to anybody even to his or her parents, guardians, siblings and relatives without his or her permission. Any person who wishes to get a student’s school records must secure special power of attorney (SPA) before the school will entertain the request.
 
SECTION VII.
Violations, Disciplinary, and Intervention Measures
A.	CLASSIFICATIONS OF OFFENSES

1.	Major Offenses
1.1.	Category A
Students who are found responsible for committing major offense under category A are subject for expulsion. The following are examples of offenses under this category:

1.1.1.	Using, possessing, distributing or peddling illegal drugs or hallucinogenic agents;
1.1.2.	Carrying deadly weapons, firearms, explosives and components thereof, as well as knife or bolo within the school campus, except if they are being used for class purposes and approved by school authorities;
1.1.3.	Direct assault upon any member of the school community or grave threats to inflict harm on other's life or property such as death threats, Hostage Taking, kidnapping and black−mail of any forms;
1.1.4.	Molesting or sexually harassing someone in the school campus.
1.1.5.	Stealing money from any person or from the funds of the organizations, test papers, reports and other school records.
1.1.6.	Forging or altering documents like admission slips, transcript of records, honorable dismissal, examination permits, clearances, official receipts;
1.1.7.	Malversation	of	funds of	the	school	clubs and organizations and the like;
1.1.8.	Leading or participating in illegal or unauthorized assemblies and/or strikes;
1.1.9.	Harassing the school community or picketing at the entrance or exit of the College;
 
1.1.10.	Immoral and vulgar sexual acts inside or outside the campus such as:
a.	Pre−marital sex
b.	Prostitution
c.	Having sexual activities with members of the same sex or gender
1.1.11.	Hazing of any kind either inside or outside of the school campus or recruitment of a student to join any unrecognized organization, fraternity, sorority that practices hazing;
1.1.12.	Libel or malicious defamation expressed either in writing, printing or by signs or pictures which clearly demeans the dignity of the person;
1.1.13.	Acts of subversion, insurgency, insurrection or rebellion including possession or distribution of subversive materials.;
1.1.14.	Final conviction before any court for a criminal offense;
1.1.15.	All acts committed by any student in violation of the Revised Penal Code of the Philippines; and
1.1.16.	Any crime or misdemeanor committed by the students not found in this handbook but is considered by the Student Disciplinary Board as under this category.

1.2.	Category B
Students who are found responsible for committing major offense under category B are subject for exclusion. The following are examples of offenses under this category:
1.2.1.	Fighting or any violent acts causing physical injury and group fighting;
1.2.2.	An act of conspiring together to dishonor or malign the school and its personnel or his/her fellow students either in speech, writing or through the use of social media;
1.2.3.	Bringing of alcoholic drinks without permission from the school authorities and drinking or being intoxicated with liquor;
1.2.4.	Vandalism and destruction of school property, like tearing off or defacing any school documents such as books, journals, reports and the like, writing or carving or drawing on the walls and furniture and the like;
1.2.5.	Forcible entry into the College campus;
 
1.2.6.	Unauthorized collection of money or other instruments used as equivalent for money from other students or any member of the school community;
1.2.7.	Consistent disregard or willful infringement of established policies, rules and regulations consisting in the commission of three (3) minor transgressions of the same kind or nature, or five (5) minor transgressions of different kinds or nature;
1.2.8.	Willful failure to comply with summons or notices issued for purposes of investigation conducted in relation with discipline−related misdemeanors;
1.2.9.	Publication or circulation of false and inaccurate information about his/her fellow students or about the school and its school personnel;
1.2.10.	Possession and distribution of libelous publications, writings or other materials;
1.2.11.	Showing, exhibiting or exposing nudity or nakedness in print media and social media such as youtube, facebook and others which causes scandal to the school and the school community;
1.2.12.	Bribing or accepting bribe from fellow student or school personnel in exchange of grades and other favors;
1.2.13.	Threatening, terrorizing or intimidating any person in the school community;
1.2.14.	Sending emails or posting comments with the intent of scaring, hurting, or intimidating someone else including cyber bullying; and
1.2.15.	Any crime or misdemeanor committed by the students not found in these lists but is considered by the Student Disciplinary Board as under this category.

1.3.	Category C
Students who are found responsible for committing major offense under category C are subject for suspension or other sanctions as determined by the Student Disciplinary Board. The following are examples of offenses under this category:
1.3.1.	Dishonesty like cheating during examination, stealing money intended for tuition without the knowledge of the parents and benefactors;
 
1.3.2.	Gambling in any form inside the campus.
1.3.3.	Smoking inside the campus or at least within 100 meters from the campus. (CMO No. 63, S. 2007);
1.3.4.	Staying on the campus beyond the curfew hours or overnight without permission from the school authorities;
1.3.5.	Public display of intimate and amorous gestures that cause scandal to other students and school personnel;
1.3.6.	Possession or distribution of pornographic materials;
1.3.7.	Using another person's ID, lending ID to another, using two or more IDs;
1.3.8.	Not reporting to contest participated by the school without valid reason and approval of the school authorities;
1.3.9.	Maligning the Catholic Church, her teachings and practices as well as her ministers; and
1.3.10.	Any crime or misdemeanor committed by the students not found in these lists but is considered by the Student Disciplinary Board as under this category.

2.	Minor Offenses - Suspension
The following are considered minor offenses:

2.1.	Violating the campus dress code;
2.2.	Failure to wear the ID inside the campus;
2.3.	Posting of unauthorized notices, announcements on boards or posting of announcements outside the authorized bulletin board;
2.4.	Throwing of garbage outside the trashcans;
2.5.	Unauthorized use of bulletin boards;
2.6.	Loitering in corridors during class sessions;
2.7.	Putting up of feet on chairs and tables or sitting on the arm of the chair.
2.8.	Improper use of cellular phones and other electronic devices during class sessions;
2.9.	Wearing of earrings/face rings for men inside the campus;
2.10.	Wearing of face rings or multiple earrings for women;
2.11.	Unauthorized removal or tampering of notices posted for information;
2.12.	Representing the school in meetings or conferences without authorization;
 
2.13.	Wearing or using important identification or symbol of the school such as banner, zeal or using the name of the school without permission;
2.14.	Unauthorized use of school property and equipment;
2.15.	Use of classrooms and other school facilities for any purpose without any reservation or proper authorization;
2.16.	Smoking including e−cigarettes inside the school premises;
2.17.	Selling items, engaging in business or soliciting contributions or donations in campus without prior approval of authority; and
2.18.	Any crime or misdemeanor committed by the students not found in these lists but is considered by the Student Disciplinary Board as under this category.

B.	SANCTIONS
The following are the general sanctions to be imposed to students who are found liable or accountable for an offense:

1.	Expulsion. The sanction imposed to a student liable of an offense by excluding him/her from admission to any public or private school in the country;
2.	Exclusion. The sanction imposed to a student liable of an offense by simply dropping his/her name from the roll of the college students for being undesirable;
3.	Suspension. The sanction imposed to a student liable of an offense by depriving him/her to enter the school for a period of time;
4.	Disqualification from holding or seeking any position in the student government or clubs and organizations;
5.	Disqualification to join in different school competitions and other extra−curricular activities;
6.	Removal from school's scholarship in case the responsible student is a scholar; and
7.	Not allowing the student to participate in graduation ceremonies and related activities if he/she is a graduating student under disciplinary intervention procedure.
 
C.	FORMATIVE INTERVENTION PROCESS
The following are the corrective measures and formative intervention processes for students who are found responsible / liable of an offense:
1.	For Expulsion Category
1.1.	Submission of letter of apology to the Prefect of Student Formation;
1.2.	Counseling session with the Guidance Counselor;
1.3.	Payment for actual damage of property/facility or any offense involving money (if applicable); and
1.4.	Dismissal from the roster of the College.

2.	For Exclusion Category
2.1.	Submission of letter of apology to the Prefect of Student Formation;
2.2.	Payment for actual damage of property/facility or any offense involving money (if applicable);
2.3.	Suspension from attending classes for two (2) weeks;
2.4.	Community service for 120 hours to be coursed through the Br. Polycarp Community Development Foundation;
2.5.	Individual or personal learning activity at the library during days of class suspension;
2.6.	Submission of reflection paper to the Guidance and Counseling Center; and
2.7.	Counseling Session with the Guidance Counselor.

3.	For Suspension Category
3.1.	Submission of letter of apology to the Prefect of Student Formation;
3.2.	Payment for actual damage of property/facility or any offense involving money (if applicable);
3.3.	Suspension from attending classes for five (5) days;
3.4.	Community Service for 40 hours to be coursed through the Br. Polycarp Community Development Foundation;
3.5.	Individual or personal learning activity at the library during days of class suspension;
3.6.	Submission of reflection paper to the Guidance and Counseling Center; and
3.7.	Counseling Session with the Guidance Counselor.
 
4.	For Minor Offenses
4.1.	First Offense
4.1.1.	Submission of letter of apology to the Prefect of Student Formation;
4.1.2.	Suspension from attending classes for two (2) days;
4.1.3.	Payment for actual damage of property/facility or any offense involving money (if applicable);
4.1.4.	Community Service for 8 hours to be coursed through the Prefect of Student Formation;
4.1.5.	Individual or personal learning activity at the library during days of class suspension;
4.1.6.	Submission of reflection paper to the Guidance and Counseling Center; and
4.1.7.	Counseling Session with the Guidance Counselor
4.2.	Second Offense
4.2.1	Submission of letter of apology to the Prefect of Student Formation;
4.2.2	Suspension from attending classes for Five (5) days
4.2.3	Payment for actual damage of property/facility or any offense involving money (if applicable);
4.2.4	Community Service for 12hours to be coursed through the Prefect of Student Formation;
4.2.5	Individual or personal learning activity at the library during days of class suspension;
4.2.6	Submission of reflection paper to the Guidance and Counseling Center; and
4.2.7	Counseling Session with the Guidance Counselor

4.3.	Third Offense
4.3.1.	Submission of letter of apology to the Prefect of Student Formation;
4.3.2.	Suspension from attending classes for ten (10) days
4.3.3.	Payment for actual damage of property/facility or any offense involving money (if applicable);
4.3.4.	Community Service for 16hours to be coursed through the Br. Polycarp Community Development Foundation;
4.3.5.	Individual or personal learning activity at the Library during days of class suspension;
4.3.6.	Submission of reflection paper to the Guidance and Counseling Center; and
 
4.3.7.	Counseling Session with the Guidance Counselor.

For fourth offense and above, formative intervention for exclusion category shall be applied.

D.	DETERMINING THE VIOLATION

1.	The faculty members have the right to evaluate and censure their students for any minor violation;
2.	With regard to academic matters, the Dean of College assumes the responsibility of determining the nature of the offense committed by the student;
3.	The Student Disciplinary Board, upon the recommendation of the Prefect of Student Formation, shall have the duty to hear and decide the cases. The decision of the Board may be appealed to the Office of the President; and
4.	The evaluation of the violation will be based on the mitigating and aggravating circumstances and evidences to be determined by the Student Disciplinary Board.

E.	JURISDICTION OF THE CASES
1.	Academic problems: College Dean
2.	Faculty problems: College Dean
3.	Non−academic and other problems of students: Director for Student Services

F.	STUDENT DISCIPLINARY BOARD

1.	Functions and duties
1.1.	Investigates cases referred by the Prefect of Student Formation and within its jurisdiction;
1.2.	Recommends sanctions for the accused to the President of the School; and
1.3.	Submits policy recommendations (crafting, innovation, improvement) to the Director of Student Services pertaining to student discipline and decorum of the school.
 
2.	Composition
2.1.	Director for Student Services as chairperson
2.2.	Dean of College (Vice−Chairperson)
2.3.	Prefect of Student Formation
2.4.	Representative from the faculty
2.5.	Representative from the staff
2.6.	Guidance Counselor
2.7.	CSG President or his/her representative

3.	Procedural Due Process
3.1.	The student must be informed in writing of the nature and cause of the accusation against him/her;
3.2.	The student must be informed of his/her right to answer the charges against him/her, with the assistance of a counsel, if desired;
3.3.	The student must be told of the evidence against him/her;
3.4.	The student must be told of his/her right to present evidence for his/her own behalf;
3.5.	Evidences must be considered by the Student Disciplinary Board; and
3.6.	Upon completion of the investigation, the student must be informed about the findings and recommendations of the members of the board. He/she will also be informed of her right to make an appeal about the decision to be submitted to the school president. If a student is a minor, his or her parents are required to attend during the hearing and other meetings. If the student is of legal age, his or parents can participate in the hearing and investigation upon request and with the approval of the student.

G.	PREGNANT STUDENTS
For Pregnant Students who are given consideration by the Student Disciplinary Board (SDB) to continue their studies in school, the following must be complied:

1.	Letter of intent to continue schooling noted by the parents or guardian;
2.	Conference with the Prefect together the parent or guardian;
3.	Notarized affidavit of waiver, relinquishing one’s right for any claim and
releasing liability of the school whenever there be untoward incident
 
that might happened during the course of pregnancy while continuing the schooling;
4.	Medical Certificate signifying fitness to undergo any tedious or strenuous activity in the school (every month); and
5.	Counseling session with the Guidance Counselor to cater and assess
one’s psycho−emotional condition and the like.
 
SECTION VIII.
Organizations and Interest Clubs
Organizations and Interest Clubs are duly accredited by the school to provide avenue for students to harness their talents, integrate the core values of the institution and develop their potentials for compassionate leadership.
A.	CLASSIFICATIONS OF ORGANIZATIONS AND INTEREST CLUBS

1.	Religious Organizations (Non-Academic Organizations)
These are organizations that promote the teachings of the Catholic Church and the Charism of the Brothers of the Sacred Heart. They assist the Sacred Heart Formation and Mission Office in the liturgical and other spiritual formation of the students, the school personnel and the whole school community. They also provide services to communities outside CJC.
2.	Socio-Civic Organizations (Non-Academic Organizations)
These organizations develop students to be socially responsible, culturally literate, politically involved, environmentally educated and community immersed making them witnesses of the compassionate love of God. Thus, they also help the school community in reaching out to those persons in need of their help, services and expertise.

3.	Academic Organizations
These clubs provide avenues for common search for excellence in their fields of specialization through quiz bees, fora, seminars and other effective means or opportunities for academic development. They assist the college in their academic services and other activities of the students. In doing so, the members of the clubs and organizations will enhance their knowledge, skills and expertise to prepare them as effective professionals and intellectual advocates of education in society.

4.	Student Councils or Student Governments
Student Councils are the armed wing of the Student Services Center, the Colleges and the school in general in bringing the concern of the students to the administration and vice−versa. They promote student activities  that  enhance  the  leadership  and  other  skills  and
 
competencies of the students in partnership with the Student Services Center. This is the highest student organization of the school and the other clubs and organizations are under its supervision. The College Student Government exists to serve the following objectives:
4.1.	To safeguard the students' welfare in the formulation and implementation of the school policies;
4.2.	To serve as a forum of students' opinion for the improvement of the Cor Jesu College community;
4.3.	To establish rapport between the students and the administration;
4.4.	To assist the duly constituted authorities in the implementation of the school rules for the maintenance of a harmonious academic community;
4.5.	To assist the Student Services Center in the planning and implementation of non−academic activities and other extra− curricular activities designed to enhance the growth and the welfare of the students; and
4.6.	To provide the students with opportunities for a healthy interaction needed in the building of a harmonious community.

B.	REQUIREMENTS FOR ACCREDITATION OF CLUBS AND ORGANIZATIONS
1.	Each organization must have a Constitution and By−laws;
2.	The objectives of the organization/club must be aligned with the Vision, Mission, Goals and Objectives of the College Department;
3.	The organization/club must have a moderator(s), who is/are employed in Cor Jesu College. Their designation must be approved by the Director of Student Services; and
4.	The organization/club must submit a list of moderator(s), officers, members, Operational or Action Plans (with proposed budget), Calendar of Activities as well as proposed projects and research for the whole year.
 
C.	REQUIREMENTS FOR AFFILIATED CLUBS AND ORGANIZATIONS

The organization/club that has local, regional or national affiliation may be accredited as a legitimate group of the school provided that the following requirements are complied with:
1.	Manual for the Standard Training Procedure that includes all the rituals used for accepting members;
2.	Notarized statement that hazing of any form is not used for acceptance of members;
3.	Organizational chart which the club/group is affiliated with;
4.	List of officers of the organization which the club is affiliated; and
5.	Compliance with the requirements as listed above.
D.	PROCEDURES ON ACCREDITATION OF ORGANIZATIONS

1.	Filing out of Application form;
2.	Submission of accomplished application form at the Student Services Center with attachments of the requirements within fifteen (15) days from the start of regular class;
3.	Assessment of submitted documents by Student Activity Coordinator within ten (10) days from the date of deadline of submission;
4.	The Student Activity Coordinator endorses application to the Student Services Council for the approval and official recognition;
5.	Sending of evaluation results and issuance of certificate of recognition or accreditation to the respective organization;
6.	In case of dis−accreditation, there will be an appeal period for five (5) working days and comply the following:
6.1.	The concerned student organization must submit a formal letter of appeal to the Student Activity Coordinator.
6.2.	The Student Activity Coordinator shall act on the appeal within three (3) working days from the receipt of the appeal. During this period the officers of the concerned organization may be invited for a dialogue.
6.3.	The Student Activity Coordinator shall communicate the decision to the concerned organization through a formal letter.
 
E.	REQUIREMENTS FOR RE-ACCREDITATION OF CLUBS AND ORGANIZATIONS
1.	A club or organization is re−accredited if the following requirements are compiled:
1.1.	Operational Plans and Budgets
1.2.	Annual Performance Reports
1.3.	Financial Reports
1.4.	Lists of New Officers and Members and moderator
1.5.	Updated Constitution and by−laws (if any)
2.	A club that cannot comply with the above requirements for the set deadline will be informed about their deficit and will be given extension; and
3.	In case the clubs or organizations cannot submit the required documents for re−accreditation after the extended period, they will be put in a probationary status for one year. If after a year, they cannot still submit the required documents, they will be removed from the lists of accredited clubs and organizations.

F.	QUALIFICATIONS OF OFFICERS AND MEMBERS
1.	Only bona fide students currently enrolled in the College Department may become officers and members;
2.	Officers must have a minimum load of 15 units every semester.
3.	They must be students of Cor Jesu College for at least one semester prior to the holding of office;
4.	Officers could handle major positions in only two organizations or clubs except the presidency. A president of an interest club or organization cannot handle the same position with other interest club or organization; and
5.	Officers who have not been sanctioned by the school for any major infraction of school regulations are eligible for any position.
 
G.	ELECTION OF CLUB/ORGANIZATION OFFICERS

1.	The election of the College Student Government (CSG) should be guided by the approved CSG−COMELEC guidelines and is conducted at the later part of the second semester;
2.	The election of the organization officers should be governed by their approved Constitution and By−laws and is conducted at the later part of the second semester; and
3.	The election must be conducted at the end of the second semester.
H.	FUNCTIONS OF OFFICERS AND MEMBERS

1.	The responsibilities of the organization and club officers and members must be clearly indicated in the constitution and by−laws;
2.	Officers must submit activity and financial reports to the Student Services Center one week after the activity;
3.	Officers are required to submit an annual evaluation and terminal reports of activities as well as a compilation of the liquidation of financial expenses to the Student Services Center before the final examinations;
4.	Officers are required to submit operational or action plans (with proposed budget), calendar of activities, proposed projects and research, lists of new officers and members for the following year on the first month of the opening of the first semester; and
5.	Officers and members are required to attend the approved activities of the Association of College Clubs and Organization (ACCO), College Student Government (CSG), and Student Services Center (SSC).
I.	MODERATORS
Advisorship or moderatorship is an important function of a school personnel in the leadership development of the students.

1.	The Moderator must be an employee of Cor Jesu College;
2.	He/She is nominated by the club officers and approved by the Director for Student Services;
3.	The Moderator gives technical assistance and guidance to the club;
4.	He/She endorses the activities and projects of the club to the Director for Student Services;
 
5.	He/She must read and scrutinize the activities, projects and budget of the officers and members of the clubs before endorsing them to the Director for Student Services;
6.	He/She has the power to disapprove the activities and requests of the officers and members;
7.	All−important communications of the organization require the perusal and signature of the Moderator;
8.	Motivating the officers and members to attain the goals and objectives of the club is a vital role of the moderator; and
9.	The Moderator attends every major activity of the club especially overnight and off−campus activity.

J.	RECORDS OF ORGANIZATIONS
1.	The organizations and clubs must keep their own records of the Constitution and By−Laws, minutes of meetings, activity, annual, terminal and financial reports;
2.	They are allowed to collect reasonable registration fee to be used as funds for their approved activities. However, they have to inform the Director for Student Services in writing about such plan to collect registration fees;
3.	They may organize creative activities to raise funds for the organizations and clubs except solicitation;
4.	The organization and club's expenses must be well−recorded and supported with official or temporary receipts;
5.	The organizations/clubs are allowed to hold a petty cash fund as specified by the Student Services Center. The excess amount must be deposited in the bank of their choice or in the Finance Office for safekeeping. In case they choose to deposit their money in the banks, they must follow the following guidelines:

5.1.	The bankbook must be deposited in the Student Services Center. The officers can borrow the bankbook only when they need to withdraw or deposit money with the approval of the moderator.
5.2.	The signatories should not be less than the following: moderator, president and the treasurer.
6.	If the club or organization chooses to deposit their money at the Finance Office, the receipt of money deposited in the Finance Office must be submitted to the Student Services Center.
 
K.	ACTIVITIES AND PROJECTS

1.	Activities of organizations must be endorsed by the moderator and approved by the Director for Student Services;
2.	Clubs or organizations are allowed to hold major on−campus activities provided that they comply with the following requirements:
2.1.	The officers of the club must submit activity proposal, program design, minutes of the meeting, list of participants, budget proposal (if any), resolution, photocopy of the approved venue/facility booking form to the Student Services Center;
2.2.	The club officers are required to fill out booking forms for the use of school facilities and have them signed by persons in authority;
2.3.	The club officers must submit Operational Guidelines for Health and Safety Protocol duly signed by Safety and Security Officer and School Nurse;
2.4.	The activity will only be up to 5:00 in the afternoon. Activities beyond the intended time are subject for approval of the Director for Student Services. Moreover, officers must seek approval from the Vice President for Finance and Administration for extension of the use of the venue/facility. In case of overnight stay, the officers of the club are required to get an approval from the President of the School; and
2.5.	The organizations and clubs are required to return borrowed equipment and furniture, and are responsible for the restoration of venue or area after the activity. Failure to do these is a ground for investigation and possible cancellation of the club or organization’s right to conduct an activity. Officers of the club or organization might also face disciplinary measures.
3.	Student organizations and clubs are allowed to conduct off−campus activities provided that the following requirements are complied with:

3.1.	The officers of the club should submit to the Student Services Center an activity proposal and program design attached with the flow of activities endorsed by the moderator or adviser;
3.2.	The officers should secure a notarized affidavit of consent forms for all participants to be endorsed by the Advisers or Moderators, noted by the Dean of College and approved by the Director for Student Services. The parent or guardian must sign it and the return slip should be submitted to the moderator or adviser. The
 
moderator or adviser shall give a photocopy of the signed parent consent to the Student Services Center before they are allowed to leave the campus for their off−campus activities;
3.3.	The club officers must submit Operational Guidelines for Health and Safety Protocol duly signed by Safety and Security Officer and School Nurse;
3.4.	The moderator or his/her authorized representative should accompany the group during the whole activity. The club or organization/class is required to have 1 teacher/moderator per 30 students/participants. Personnel−in−charge must have appropriate first−aid and medical emergency training;
3.5.	The officers should secure medical clearance of the participants;
3.6.	The officers should request a complete first−aid kit from the school clinic; and
3.7.	The officers should book a trip ticket from the General Services Office duly signed by the persons in authority. In case of a sub− contracting vehicle, photocopies of certification from LTFRB for the validity of the franchise of the proposed operator (i. e. legitimate and up−to−date), if applicable, special permit from LTFRB if transportation is out−of−line, updated/valid documents pertaining to registration, insurance coverage, driver’s license, and assurance of roadworthiness.

L.	SANCTIONS
1.	An organization and/or club that has violated any provision of the College Student Handbook and state laws will be investigated by those in authority. If found guilty, the organization or club will automatically be suspended for a maximum of three years;
2.	Any officer or member of the club who has violated school policies and state laws will be investigated. If found guilty, the following will be imposed:

1.1.	The officers or members will be removed from office or from the organization.
1.2.	The school may impose sanctions based on Section 7 of the College Student Handbook.
 
3.	Any damage to school property and equipment will be charged to offending individuals or parties, without prejudice of being investigated and given administrative sanctions based on Section 7 of the College Student Handbook;
4.	The damaged equipment must be replaced with the same equipment; or else, the organization/club or individual will be charged the total cost according to the current price of the damaged equipment or property;
5.	The school reserves the right to approve, suspend and dissolve clubs and organizations. The organization and/or club is suspended or dissolved when found guilty of any of the following:

5.1.	If the activity in the name of the club is an infraction of the rules of the College; and
5.2.	If the club violates its Constitution and By−laws or the laws of the country.
 
SECTION IX.
Co-Curricular and Extra-Curricular Activities
A.	CO-CURRICULAR ACTIVITIES
Co−curricular activities are outside classroom activities organized and spearheaded by the subject teachers and are intended to complement classroom instruction for the enhancement of skills, assimilation of values, and broadening of understanding of concepts, theories and principles. These may include but not limited to the following:
1.	Seminar−workshops
2.	Spiritual Activities
3.	Symposia or Fora
4.	Socio−cultural and Athletic Competitions
5.	Academic Contests
6.	Field Trips
7.	Exposures or Community Immersions
B.	EXTRA-CURRICULAR ACTIVITIES
Extra−curricular activities are those that contribute to the total development of the students and are organized by the school, other institutions or recognized organizations and clubs and other groups that are approved by the administration. Presented in the table below are some of the examples of these activities.
Socio-Cultural Events	Sports Events	Campus Writing and Aesthetic
Competitions	Developmental & Environmental
Activities
Vocal Solo Duet Chorus Folk Dance
Ethic Dance Ethno Jazz
Interpretative Dance Cheer Dance
Dance Theater Popular dance Sayawitan Pista sa Nayon Band Concert Theatre
Visual Arts	Basketball Volleyball Softball Baseball Sepak−Takraw Taekwondo Badminton Table Tennis Chess
Games of the General Scrabble
Word Factory Dart
Lawn Tennis Swimming
Frisbee Athletic Events	Painting Contest Essay−writing Debate
Song Composition Drama
Presentations Techno−graphics Poetry interpretation Oratorical contests Impromptu
Radio Broadcasting News Casting Hosting Modeling	Seminars Conventions Clean−up Drives Parades
Tree Growing Bird Monitoring Nature Tripping
Camping & training Community−based Research Mountain Climbing Fun run
 
1.	INTRAMURAL ACTIVITIES
1.1.	Intramural activities will be conducted for only three days excluding Saturday and Sunday. School days before and after are considered class days;
1.2.	The College Student Government (CSG) and the College Department Officers should not consume all the collected Student Activity Fund (SAF) for the Intramural Activities only. The SAF is also intended for curricular and extra−curricular activities for students’ holistic enhancement;
1.3.	The Mini−Olympics which is usually held prior to the conduct of the intramural activities is held only whenever it is necessary for the Colleges to select their players and contestants for the intramural activities. The Colleges are only allowed to withdraw 10% of the collected College Standing Fund during the first semester to finance the expenses of the activity;
1.4.	The props, costumes, uniforms of the participants for competitions especially for intramural games should be governed by the following:
1.4.1.	The College where the players or contestants belong may, or should share 50% of the costumes and uniform of the participants.
1.4.2.	The t−shirt uniform for students during intramural activities and foundation days will only be on voluntary basis.
1.5.	Costumes and props for the intramural activities may be rented provided that the price involved is reasonable; and
1.6.	The use of harmful objects such as firecrackers, explosives, or burning objects that can cause fire is strictly prohibited.

2.	OTHER ACTIVITIES
Any group of students can organize other school activities not in the list provided that the activities are not contrary to school rules and are duly approved by the Director for Student Services.

C.	TRAINERS, REFEREES, AND JUDGES FOR COMPETITIONS
1.	The school discourages hiring of trainers outside of Cor Jesu College;
2.	The school encourages the selection of judges from Cor Jesu College. The honoraria for trainers and judges must be within the approved rate set by the school;
3.	If and when circumstances would call for the organizer to invite judges and trainers from outside the school, letter of request signifying the names and qualifications of judges and trainers must be submitted to
 
the Student Services Center for approval. Moreover, Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) or Memorandum of Agreement (MOA) which includes the agreed amount of trainers’ fee the scope of the job and the duration of the training must also be submitted for approval to the Director for Student Services; and
4.	The referees for the basketball and volleyball games shall be the varsity players, except for championship games where outside referees may be hired.

D.	PRACTICES OF PRESENTATIONS

1.	The practice or rehearsal of presentations shall be done only on the school campus, except for tune−up games that may be held outside the campus;
2.	The practices shall not go beyond 5:00 o'clock in the evening and shall not be earlier than 4:00 0'clock in the morning;
3.	The students must book the place and the equipment to be used ahead of time;
4.	If and when circumstances would call for the organizer to hold practices outside the school, the organizer must submit the following to the Director for Student Services for approval;
4.1.	Letter indicating the date, time and venue of practices;
4.2.	Letter of approval from the authorized persons of the selected venue;
4.3.	Agreed amount of payment or rent of the place and venue;
4.4.	Safety Guidelines and Health Protocols;
4.5.	List of Participants;
4.6.	Parent’s Consent of the Participants

E.	REQUIREMENTS FOR OFF-CAMPUS ACTIVITIES

1.	The following are required for off−campus activities, like immersion, field trip, recollection, retreat, exposure, camping, swimming, seminar, conventions and others:
1.1.	Letter from the Organizer
1.2.	Activity Proposal
1.3.	Program Design with Activity Flow
1.4.	Minutes of the Meeting
1.5.	Budget Proposal
1.6.	Resolution (if applicable)
1.7.	List of Participants
 
1.8.	Approved House Rules − Health and Safety Protocol duly signed by School Nurse and Safety and Security Officer
1.9.	Notarized Affidavit of Consent
1.10.	Parent’s Consent
1.11.	Medical Certificate
1.12.	Trip ticket from the General Services Office duly signed by the persons in authority. In case of a sub−contracting vehicle, photocopies of certification from LTFRB for the validity of the franchise of the proposed operator (i. e. legitimate and up−to− date), if applicable, special permit from LTFRB if transportation is out−of−line, updated/valid documents pertaining to registration, insurance coverage, driver’s license, and assurance of roadworthiness.
2.	There must be a presence of Lifeguards and/or Safety Officer during outdoor activities especially for swimming, camping, community immersion, mountain climbing and the like; and
3.	Organization officers, moderators and/or teachers accompanying the students must ensure that the requirements are complied. Moreover, they have to check the condition of the vehicles and other means of transportation that they will use in transporting students to the desired venues of the activities.

F.	REQUIREMENTS FOR ON-CAMPUS ACTIVITIES
1.	The following are required for on−campus activities:
1.1.	Activity Proposal
1.2.	Program Design with Activity Flow
1.3.	Minutes of the Meeting
1.4.	Budget Proposal
1.5.	Resolution
1.6.	Approved House Rules – Health and Safety Protocol duly signed by School Nurse and Safety and Security Officer
1.7.	List of Participants
1.8.	Booking of facilities/equipment needed
1.9.	Parent’s Consent, if on−campus activity is conducted beyond 5:00 pm
2.	The activity must always start with a prayer or Eucharistic celebration, followed by the singing of the Philippine National Anthem, Cor Jesu College Hymn, the recitation of the Vision, Mission and Core Value of the school; and
 
3.	The theme of the program must always be anchored on the annual institutional theme.

G.	PROCEDURES FOR APPROVAL OF ACTIVITIES
1.	Fill out activity proposal form and submit to the Student Services Center with attachments of required documents at least five (5) working days before the activity;
2.	For off−campus and overnight activities, parent's consent of participants is required;
3.	For overnight activities in the campus, organizers must secure approval from the Office of the President;
4.	The procedures in the signing of the parent's consent are as follows:
4.1.	The Moderator or Adviser, Dean of the Department, Dean of College, Director of Students Services, Parent or Guardian and student must sign the Parent’s Consent Form; and
4.2.	The Moderator or Adviser distributes the Parent's Consent Forms and thereafter collects them from the participants. Student will not be allowed to join the activity without parent’s consent.
5.	The organizers must secure copy of the approved activity proposal at the Student Services Center before conducting the activity.
H.	ATTENDANCE OF STUDENTS IN VARIOUS ACTIVITIES
1.	The students are required to participate in on and off−campus activities as may be required by those in authority;
2.	The students who are absent during the required activity shall be considered absent in all the enrolled subjects of that day;
3.	The school does not allow the imposition of fines as a punishment due to absences during the required activity; and
4.	The moderators should be present during meetings and other activities to provide guidance to the students and to monitor the implementation of activities or events.

I.	BEHAVIOR OF STUDENTS DURING ON AND OFF-CAMPUS ACTIVITIES
1.	Students are not allowed to utter vulgar words and green jokes during presentations. Words that desecrate and blaspheme the Lord, and expressions that malign the Church, the Institution, or any person in the community are taboo;
2.	Any misconduct or misbehavior of participants and students during the show or presentation, like howling, shouting, unnecessary noise and other behavior will be dealt with accordingly; and
 
3.	Students who are under the influence of liquor and prohibited drugs will not be allowed to participate in the activity without prejudice of being investigated and given appropriate sanction according to existing rules of the school.
J.	BUDGET AND LIQUIDATION OF FUNDS
1.	The organizing group should prepare a budget and secure an approval from the Director for Student Services;
2.	The liquidation of funds must be done one week after the holding of the activity and it must be supported with official or temporary receipts;
3.	A person given an honorarium should sign a voucher where the amount received is indicated. This is countersigned by the disbursing officer;
4.	The organizer must limit expenses according to the budget approved by the Director for Student Services. In case of a deficit, the organizer should get the approval of the Director for Student Services for additional funds;
5.	The auditor, treasurer, chairperson, president and the moderator or adviser should sign the financial report;
6.	Any remaining funds should be re−deposited to the Finance Office or the bank; and
7.	Celebrations outside or inside the school after any institutional activity using the funds of the club, organization, college must have approval from the Director for Student Services.
K.	RESTORATION AFTER ACTIVITIES
1.	Organizers should return borrowed materials and equipment to their respective places or offices right after the activity;
2.	They should take care of the borrowed property or equipment. Any damage or loss incurred due to negligence will be subjected to replacement or payment of the actual value of the equipment based on the Finance Office assessment;
3.	They should remove decorations, props, and other materials used during the activity; and
4.	They should also clean the venue after the conduct of the activity.
 
L.	DISAPPROVAL OF ACTIVITIES
The school reserves the right to disapprove activities or events organized by the College Student Government or Student clubs and organizations if they contain one of the following:
1.	The activities are contrary to the core value and beliefs upheld by the College;
2.	The activity is very expensive and detrimental to the well−being of the students and the school as a whole;
3.	The activities are against the constitution of the club, the policies and rules of the school and the laws of the country; and
4.	If the organizations are caught violating the provisions of this handbook and found guilty of deliberately doing such or of negligence of duty such as cleaning the venue after the events and the like.
 
SECTION X.
Non-Academic Awards
The following are the non−academic awards to be given to graduating students who have excelled in various areas of student life. The awards are classified as:
A.	INSTITUTIONAL AWARDS

1.	FR. ANDRE COINDRE LEADERSHIP AWARD
1.1.	Guidelines
To be eligible for the award, a nominee must satisfy all of the following guidelines:
1.1.1.	A member of the graduating class
1.1.2.	Continued residence for the last three years
1.1.3.	Has no failing mark in the final grades in academic and non− academic subjects for the last three years
1.1.4.	Has no dropped subject for the last two years
1.1.5.	Has not been found guilty of any violations of the rules of the institution on and off campus for the current School Year
1.1.6.	Has been an elected officer of any recognized school organization for the last three years
1.1.7.	Has completed the program within the prescribed number of years

1.2.	Criteria
To be given the award, a nominee must get a total of at least 85% of the following criteria:
1.2.1.	Leadership skills and qualities (40%)
1.2.2.	Academic Performance (20%)
1.2.3.	Non−academic Performance on−campus (20%)
1.2.4.	Non−academic Performance off−campus (20%)

2.	BR. POLYCARP COMMUNITY SERVICE AWARD
2.1.	Guidelines
To be eligible for the award, a nominee must satisfy all of the following guidelines:
2.1.1.	A member of the graduating class
 
2.1.2.	Continued residence for the last three years
2.1.3.	Has not been found guilty of any campus violation of the rules during the current school year
2.1.4.	Has no dropped subjects and/or failing marks in the final grades in academic and non−academic subjects for the last two years
2.1.5.	Has completed the program within the prescribed number of years
2.2.	Criteria
To be given the award, a nominee must get a total of at least 85% of the following criteria:
2.2.1.	Community Services Involvement (30%)
2.2.2.	Community Projects or Services Involved, organized and implemented (30%)
2.2.3.	Attitude and Values (20%)
2.2.4.	Position held outside school (10%)
2.2.5.	Academic Performance (10%)

3.	BR. ELRIC CAMPUS MINISTRY AWARD
3.1.	Guidelines
To be eligible for the award, a nominee must satisfy all of the following guidelines:
3.1.1.	A member of the Roman Catholic Church
3.1.2.	A member of the graduating class
3.1.3.	Continued residence for the last three years
3.1.4.	Has no failing mark in the academic and non−academic subjects for the last two years
3.1.5.	Has no dropped subject for the last two years
3.1.6.	Has not been found guilty of any violation of rules on− and−off campus during the current school year
3.1.7.	Has no grade lower than 2.0 in R.S. subjects

3.2.	Criteria
To be given the award, a nominee must get a total of at least 85% of the following criteria:
3.2.1.	Personal Religiosity and Spirituality (40%)
3.2.2.	Community life (30%)
3.2.3.	Academic Performance (15%)
3.2.4.	Non−academic Performance (15%)
 
4.	BR. FRANCIS LOYALTY AWARD
4.1.	Guidelines
To be eligible for the award, a nominee must satisfy all of the following guidelines:
4.1.1.	Has completed the course in Cor Jesu College
4.1.2.	Has no failing marks in the curricular year
4.1.3.	Has not been found guilty of any violation of rules on− and−off campus during the current school year

4.2.	Criteria
To be given the award, a nominee must get a total of at least 85% of the following criteria:
4.2.1.	Has studied at Cor Jesu College since first grade through high school until the completion of a collegiate course (20%)
4.2.2.	Has taken all subjects in the institution, inclusive of those taken elsewhere due to cross−enrollment and/or study permit of not more than 9 units (10%)
4.2.3.	Has completed his course up to a limit of an additional year to the normal length of studies (10%)
4.2.4.	An active member of at least one interest campus organization or club for the last three years (10%)
4.2.5.	Has been active in academic and non−academic activities (10 %)
4.2.6.	Has exhibited proper respect and pride in being a student of Cor Jesu College (20%)
4.2.7.	Has integrated the values of prayerfulness, service, commitment and compassion to others (20%)
B.	SPECIAL AWARDS

1.	OUTSTANDING INTEREST ORGANIZATION

To be eligible for the award, a nominee must satisfy all of the following guidelines:

1.1.4.	Has not been found guilty of violating school rules by causing to implement an activity contrary to school rules, laws and ordinances.
