C.	PROCEDURES ON THE SELECTION OF AWARDEES

1.	Students/organizations may only apply for the category of award which he/she thinks is suited for himself/herself. Multiple application is discouraged not unless the applicant really suffices the guidelines and requirement, thus, deserving of many awards.
2.	Applicants should obtain endorsement from the moderator, duly noted by the college dean.
3.	Applicants should fill out the application form available at the Student Services Office. The application form contains the following parts:

3.1.	Guidelines. To be eligible for the award, applicants must satisfy all the guidelines. Applicants should indicate in the application form the corresponding label of appendices as compliance to the required guidelines. Certification as proof of compliance must be obtained from the following offices:
3.1.1.	The Registrar for items pertaining to school residency, subject dropping and grades
3.1.2.	The Prefect of Student Formation for items pertaining to records of violation of school rules
3.1.3.	The Student Activity Coordinator for items pertaining to records of student activities, leadership in the campus and association of clubs and organization.
3.2.	Criteria. Applicants should supply information accordingly and indicate corresponding number of appendices as evidences exhibiting the truthfulness of the claimed information.
3.3.	Signature of the Applicant. Applicant should see to it that the application is duly signed to confirm the veracity of the information.
3.4.	Rating. This portion is reserved for the awards committee.

4.	Applicants should see to it that award application pack is complete and submitted in due time. The award application pack contains the following:
4.1.	Application form duly filled out (as cover page)
4.2.	Endorsement letter from the moderator noted by the dean of the College
 
4.3.	Write up (essay) depicting the living out of the pillar of Excellence, Community and Apostleship
4.4.	Appendices with labels containing certifications, documents and other references as exhibits of proofs
5.	Applicants should submit the award application pack in hard copy and soft copy. Hard copy (soft bound) should be submitted to Student Activity Coordinator desk and the soft copy to cjsssc@g.cjc.edu.ph on or before the set deadline.
6.	The Non−Academic Awards Committee screens and evaluates the credentials of the nominees. The committee may decide to call on the nominee and his/her adviser / moderator for additional documents, interview and further verification. Hence, applicants and/or the moderators should make themselves available during the schedule of deliberation in case the committee asks for their presence for some inquiry and clarification.
7.	The committee endorses the lists of awardees to the Academic Council for approval by the President.
 
SECTION XI.
Academic Support Services
A.	OFFICE OF THE REGISTRAR

The Office of the Registrar is responsible for administering and safekeeping of the scholastic records of all students enrolled in the College. It preserves and maintains the integrity and confidentiality of its students' records.
1.	OBJECTIVES
The Office of the Registrar commits:
1.1.	to	handle	and	treat	students'	records	with	utmost confidentiality;
1.2.	to ensure that all files are kept up−to−date;
1.3.	to submit all documents needed by partner agencies; and
1.4.	to update personnel about the new trends and thrusts of records−keeping.

2.	SERVICES
2.1.	Record Keeping
2.1.1.	Facilitates collections of source documents, admission credentials, enforced deadlines etc.;
2.1.2.	Ensures accurate recording of data;
2.1.3.	Keeps files up−to−date;
2.1.4.	Ensures fast retrieval of student records; and
2.1.5.	Ensures safety, security and confidentiality of students' records;
2.2.	Record Processing
2.2.1.	Processes/acts on requests for student records;
2.2.2.	Ensures release of student credentials on promised date;
2.2.3.	Prepares and submits reports and observes deadlines required by government agencies; and
2.2.4.	Reconstructs lost or missing records.
2.3.	Policies on Records
2.3.1.	All records of students must be handled and treated with strict confidentiality;
2.3.2.	Access to students' records is limited only to the student concerned for student of legal age, to parents or
 
guardians where the student is under their custody especially if the student is a minor, to officials of the school for decision making, and for compliance with court orders;
2.3.3.	All financial and non−financial accountabilities of students must be cleared before any record or credential is released;
2.3.4.	No record/s or credential/s will be released to the student if his/her records on file are not complete;
2.3.5.	Requested records or credentials are to be released only to the students concerned. For failure to present himself/herself, a Special Power of Attorney (SPA) is required especially if the student is of legal age. If a student is still a minor, a parent or legal guardian can process and get the student records;
2.3.6.	Completion of grades of students must be noted first by the respective deans of the college before they are recorded in the student's permanent records;
2.3.7.	Completion of grades (NT's and INC's) must be complied within 30 days after the last day of the final examination. Beyond this period, a student must re−enroll the said subject the following semester;
2.3.8.	Correction of grades must be done before the submission of Form XIX (Promotional Report) to the CHED. Once submitted, correction is no longer allowed;
2.3.9.	Duplicated or photocopied records are not accepted as admission credentials;
2.3.10.	Certified NSO copy of the birth certificate is a requirement upon enrolment and graduation;
2.3.11.	All records and credentials issued by the office is valid only when it bears the school seal and duly signed by the School Registrar; and
2.3.12.	All records submitted are for strict safekeeping.
B.	LEARNING AND INFORMATION RESOURCE CENTER (LIRC)

The LIRC is an organization, which facilitates the interaction between people and the information they need. It is one of the institution’s principal educational resources. It is in−charge of developing and progressively improving the collection and utilization of learning resource materials
 
necessary to support and supplement the instructional, research and public service programs of the college.

1.	OBJECTIVES:

1.1	To identify and provide access to the learning resources and information services required to support the learning, teaching and research activities of the institution;
1.2	To manage the resources efficiently and effectively;
1.3	To establish an environment conducive to study which caters to multiple learning styles and for both individual and group learning;
1.4	To teach faculty, staff and students how to use the LIRC and develop their information skills;
1.5	To liaise with the administration and students to establish their needs and to cooperate with management and other college
services to meet those needs;
1.6	To provide accommodation which is suitable in terms of comfort, space, furniture, ventilation, lighting and to ensure that these are maintained in a clean and tidy condition;
1.7	To provide a customer−caring attitude at all times;
1.8	To ensure that the stack is up−to−date, relevant and in good physical condition;
1.9	To encourage the LIRC staff to be actively involved in educational/professional change; and
1.10	To provide sufficient stacks to meet normal user requirements.

2.	RULES AND REGULATIONS:
2.1	LIBRARY HOURS:

2.1.1	Main LIRC:
8:00 a.m. – 7:00 p.m. − Monday to Friday 8:00 a.m. – 5:00 p.m. − Saturday

2.1.2	Health Sciences LIRC:
8:00 a.m. – 4:00 p.m. − Monday to Friday
 
2.1.3	Law/Grad School LIRC:
8:00 a.m. – 6:00p.m. − Monday to Friday 8:00 a.m. – 5:00 p.m. − Saturday

2.2	GENERAL RULES:

2.1.1.	Faculty and students must log−in at the Library Entrance Monitoring System (LEMS) using their validated CJC identification card upon entering the library premises. They must also present their CJC identification card to the lending counters whenever any LIRC material is to be borrowed. Using other’s I.D. is strictly not allowed;
2.1.2.	Students must observe silence inside the library. Idle conversation, loud laughter and other unnecessary noise must be avoided;
2.1.3.	Students are expected to wear their school uniform during class days and any decent attire during free days. Wearing of slippers, shorts, mini−skirts, jogging pants, ripped and tattered jeans, sleeveless, crop tops and other informal outfit is not allowed;
2.1.4.	Students must deposit their bags, attaché cases, magazines, newspapers, pamphlets, leaflets, etc. must be deposited at the baggage counter. They are also advised to bring with them their money, cell phones, lap tops, jewellery, and other valuable items. The LIRC will not assume responsibility for any loss of valuable materials;
2.1.5.	LIRC users are not allowed to eat and drink inside the library, except at the Library Cafe. Tumblers and other bottled waters must be deposited at the baggage counter;
2.1.6.	LIRC users must observe cleanliness and orderliness inside the library disposing pieces of papers and other garbage, and by pushing back the library chair after using;
2.1.7.	LIRC users should set their cellular phones in silent
 
mode whenever they are inside the library premises;
2.1.8.	LIRC users who have cough and runny nose are required to wear face masks and sanitize their hands whenever they are inside the library premises;
2.1.9.	Students are advised to check out at least 15 minutes before the time for inspection to avoid congestion at the exit area.

2.3	Rules on Circulation
2.3.1	Stack and Browsing Books
a.	Students can borrow stack and browsing books for one week, renewable for another week, unless another patron puts in a request.
b.	Full−time faculty members may borrow a maximum of ten (10) books at a time for three (3) weeks, while part−time faculty may borrow a maximum of five (5) books at a time for three (3) weeks.
c.	Faculty from the Basic Education Faculty (BED), non− teaching personnel, undergraduate, law, and graduate students may borrow a maximum of two
(3) books at a time for one week.



2.3.2	Reserved Books:
a.	May be read within the reading area only. A one− hour limit reading on the reserved book is strictly imposed. LIRC users will have to return it to the counter, unless nobody puts in a request for the book.
b.	May be borrowed for overnight home study. For overnight use, books may be loaned out from 6:00p.m. to 7:00 p.m. (Mondays−Fridays) and must be returned before 8:00 a.m. of the following school day. During weekends, books may be loaned out from 4:00p.m. to 5:00 p.m. (Saturdays), and must be
 
returned not later than 8:00 a.m. of the following school day.

2.3.3	Filipiniana Books:
a.	Books in the Filipiniana section may be borrowed for overnight home study. For overnight use, books may be loaned out at 6:00p.m. to 7:00 p.m. (Mondays− Fridays) and must be returned before 8:00 a.m. of the following school day. During weekends, books may be loaned out at 4:00p.m. to 5:00 p.m. (Saturdays), and must be returned not later than 8:00 a.m. of the following school day.
2.3.4. Books for Outside Photocopy (ln case the photocopier unit is out of order):
a.	Students must fill out the photocopying slip in the circulation desk and deposit their CJC validated ID’s at the circulation counter.
b.	Students are given an allotted time of 45 minutes to photocopy books outside. Failure to return the books on time is subject to penalties.
c.	Students are advised not to photocopy the whole book, in observance with the copyright law.



2.4	Fines and Other Penalties
2.4.1	For overdue books, the following fines are levied:
a.	Books in the circulation or stack, Fil./Law and Fil. Grad.P 5.00 a day, including Saturdays, Sundays and Holidays.
b.	Reserved books – P5.00 an hour (Library hour) or any fraction thereof.
c.	Books not returned after the deadline set before the end of the semester/Christmas vacation/summer period – P10.00 a day including Saturdays, Sundays and Holidays.
 
d.	Books photocopied outside, P 5.00 for the first 5 minutes; P 2.00 for every succeeding 5 minutes or any fraction thereof.
2.4.2	Students caught stealing periodicals from the library shall pay twice the current value of the periodical stolen.
2.4.3	Lost or damage book – when a book is lost, it should be reported immediately to the librarian. However, this does not exempt the borrower from paying the fines should it become overdue. Moreover, lost or damage book must be replaced with the same book (same title and author) and pay a processing fee of P150.00.
2.4.4	Students caught violating general rule 1 shall be suspended for one week for the first offense and one month for the succeeding offenses.
2.4.5	Students caught violating the general rules no. 2, 3 & 5 shall be suspended from entering the library for 3 days for the first offense and one week for the succeeding offense.
2.4.6	Students caught violating the general rules no. 6 & 7 shall be penalized through community engagement inside the library premises.
2.4.7	Any LIRC user who shall tear, deface, mutilate or steal library property shall be reported to the SSC Office for investigation and disciplinary action by the Student Disciplinary Board.
2.4.8	Fines must be paid at the finance office.

3.	PROGRAMS AND SERVICES:

3.1	Staff Development Program. This program is designed to develop efficient and effective LIRC personnel who are committed and responsive to clientele needs. In−Service Training Programs for both professional and non−professional staff are geared towards development of skills that are needed to work effectively in hybrid library environment. Training modules for apprenticeship of
 
student assistants (SAs), and in−service training are designed to foster effective learning and development of work−related skills.

3.2	Users Services Program. This program is intended to provide and deliver information services required to support the instructional and research activities of the faculty and students through Library and Online services. It is designed to adopt and demonstrate a user−centered service mentality that directs all staff activity toward delivery of resources and services to patron in multiple modalities at appropriate time and in the format desired. The library aspires to provide the following services:

3.2.1	Circulation Service. The LIRC provides lending service to students, faculty and administrators onsite and online.
3.2.2	OPAC Assistance. The LIRC staff offers one−on−one instruction in the use of the library and its bibliographic utilities like the web OPAC, bibliographies, indexes, electronic resources, and other services. Information sources can be searched through the Online Public Access Catalog (OPAC).
3.2.3	Reading Room Service. This type of service is provided for LIRC users who intend to read, study, or consult any of the resources available in the LIRC. Reading tables, sofa sets, learning commons, discussion rooms, and carrels are provided in each section.
3.2.4	Reserve Book Provision. This service includes the provision of instructional resources that are directly in line with the present curricular and instructional programs of the school. Reserved books include textbooks and other materials that are on high demand but are few in copies. These books are intended to serve a greater number of users. Students can use the books within LIRC hours; with the option to borrow the reserve books for home use through overnight use.
3.2.5	LIRC Education and Training (Library Interns). The LIRC serves as a laboratory for learning for 4th year library science students undergoing in−campus library practicum.
 
3.2.6	Reader’s Advisory Service. This service includes guidance to LIRC users in the choice of reading materials especially in their line of interests’ onsite and remote.
3.2.7	Research Assistance. Professional assistance is given in guiding researchers in the preparation of research paper/ term paper, and in identifying the resources needed.
3.2.8	Reference and Information Service. Direct/personal assistance are provided to users in the use of reference and information resources and facilities of the library. Also, the LIRC offers email reference, electronic document delivery and chat with a librarian service through the official Facebook page of the LIRC and its website.
3.2.9	Pathfinder Service. The reference section supports the research of the faculty and students by providing pathfinders for printed and non−printed information resources available at the LIRC and on the INTERNET.
3.2.10	Faculty Book Request/Tracking. The LIRC accepts request for materials needed for the different subject areas for curricular or instructional purposes. Basically, bibliographic verification of information sources requested by faculty is conducted. A status report of materials requested is available at the technical section (whether materials requested are available, out−of−stock, temporarily out−of−stock, out−of−print, temporarily out−of− print, or not available elsewhere).
3.2.11	Document Delivery. The LIRC staff attends to requests of faculty, and administrators to deliver LIRC materials immediately needed to their respective classrooms or offices. This also includes simple requests like photocopying materials subject to LIRC rules and regulations.
3.2.12	Bibliographic Service. This service is designed to promote information literacy and develop independent library users by introducing the organization of information sources and the search strategies employed to access relevant information in an efficient, effective, and timely manner. Bibliographic instruction will be provided to faculty, students or groups requesting these services,
 
especially for those currently engaged in research through onsite and online means. The LIRC staff compiles bibliographies on various subjects and formats.
3.2.13	Book Delivery Service/Electronic Document Delivery. A new customer friendly service for our clients who cannot go out of their homes can requests through door−to−door book delivery in the community. The students just request the book that they want to borrow thru library website and FB page, provide proof of enrolment and it will be delivered straight to their doorsteps or remotely.
3.2.14	User Education. The LIRC instruction is designed to introduce the facilities, organization, services and collection of the LIRC. The orientation is conducted at the beginning of the school year to all freshmen students taking Gen Ed 1, transferees, faculty and staff in blended modality. The instruction to all GE classes is coordinated with their teachers. A preliminary instruction in research methodology, bibliography making, and search strategy (e.g.: how to do literature search, how to locate LIRC materials) are provided upon request. Also, the librarians conduct co−teaching (team teaching) with the research teachers in the proper use of citations style, APA formatting and how to select quality literature.

3.2.15	Current Awareness Services (CAS) / Selective Dissemination of Information (SDI). This service includes selection of materials that a user might need and bringing to his attention that the materials are available. A user profile is compiled that will record the interests of the users and documents are matched with user’s interest. This activity is usually called selective dissemination of information or SDI. Acquisition bulletins the record the recent acquisitions of the LIRC are posted at the Info Board, shared to the GCs of the LIRC HEIs committee, posted on the FB page and LIRC website. The library maintains up−to− date information on a given topic by posting on the bulletin display corner and the e−board for the internet.
 
3.2.16	Photocopying Services. Reprographic facilities are available in the LIRC provided by CJC Cooperative and other photocopying operators. In case of brownouts, or machine failure, assistance is provided by the staff for photocopying outside the CJC campus
3.2.17	Interlibrary Use. Under this program, faculty and students of Cor Jesu College can use the resources of PLAI−DRLC Library participating schools free of charge during Saturdays, and subject to library’s rules or regulations during school days. College, graduate students and faculty can have access to academic libraries, and high school students to school libraries only. The LIRC reciprocates this service by allowing qualified researchers from PLAI−DRLC Resource Sharing participating libraries.
3.2.18	Database Searching Assistance / Electronic Access – The LIRC offers assistance to online searching / access to electronic databases covering e−journals, e−indexes and e− abstracts, on−line bibliographies, e−books and multimedia resources. On−line access to currently subscribed databases is also available. It provides instructional sample searches and other subject guides concerning CD−ROM, electronic databases and quality Open Educational Resources (OERs).

3.2.19	Connect with a Librarian – Connect with a librarian service entails personalized assistance to our library patrons for their research and academic requirements and aims to provide Cor Jesians customized library services to cater their information needs multiple learning modality.
3.3	Collection Development Program. This program aims to develop a collection of information sources in various formats to support the curricular and educational needs of the clientele. The six components of this program are: user needs assessment, collection management policy statements, selection, acquisition, deselection or weeding, and collection evaluation.
3.4	Technical Service Program. This program is geared towards a well− organized collection of information resources for easy retrieval of
 
information. The following services are: Classification, organization, computerization of LIRC records.
3.5	Physical Plant & Facilities Improvement Program – This program is designed to provide adequate and well−furnished modern LIRC facilities for optimum use. It envisions a well−designed service area that fosters an atmosphere that is inviting and accessible, safe and secure, and an environment conducive to learning.
3.6	Community Extension Program− This program is intended to provide outreach service to adapted barangay reading centers or public elementary schools in the community to help promote the love of reading to pupils and students. The library aspires to conduct the following activities: a) organize outreach program team; b) establish reading centers; and c) conduct reading room activities such as storytelling, book talk, reading aloud, quizzers and games.

1.  SERVICE HOURS
Main Library:
8:00 a.m. – 7:00 p.m. − Mondays to Fridays 8:00 a.m. – 5:00 p.m. − Saturdays
8:00 a.m. – 12:00 nn. − Sundays

Health Sciences Library:
8:00 a.m. – 5:00 p.m. − Mondays to Fridays

C.	EDUCATIONAL TECHNOLOGY CENTER
The Educational Technology Center is a learning, service, and production center for educational media technology encompassing innovative and contemporary educational systems and methods.

1.	Objectives

1.1.	To promote awareness, use and development of educational media technology among faculty members and students;
1.2.	To implement effectively an educational media technology program for students and teachers both in the private and public sectors;
 
1.3.	To initiate innovations in education media projects, modules, and activities through linkages and coordination with other educational institutions, agencies and groups; and
1.4.	To implement educational media program or project activities to help achieve financial viability;

2.	PROGRAMS AND SERVICES

2.1	Educational Resource Technology Development
2.1.1	Media Equipment Procurement Program. This program is intended to procure and upgrade media equipment to compliment the curriculum offerings of the school.
2.1.2	Media Software Procurement Program. This program is designed to procure emerging relevant instructional materials to compliment the curriculum offerings of the school.
2.1.3	Technical Service Program. This program is geared towards a well−organized collection of audio−visual media resources for easy retrieval of information. The following technical services are: Classification and Organization, and computerization of Audio−Visual Media Records.

2.2	Academic Networking Program. The program is designed to facilitate the sharing of resources available in one department with another.


2.3	Media Literacy/ Learning Program
2.3.1	Media Enhancement Staff Program. This program is intended to provide a regular in−service training of staff to make them more effective and efficient in rendering of service.
2.3.2	Media User Education. It is designed to make teachers and students knowledgeable about the use facilities, and instructional equipment, procedures for utilization
of resources, organization of materials and services of the center.
 
2.4	Audio-Visual Services Program. This program is intended to provide and deliver services required to support the curricular needs of the faculty and students.
2.4.1	Equipment Loan Services. It provides various tools for classroom instruction, lectures and conferences.
2.4.2	Advisory Service. It provides guidance to clients in their choice of non−print materials in their line of interest.
2.4.3	Non-print Request / Tracking and Document Search. This service provides assistance to request for materials available on and off campus needed in the different subject areas for curricular or instructional purposes.
2.4.4	Bibliographic Services. The Edtech Center provides bibliographic listing of non−print materials.
2.5	Software Production Services. This program is intended to produce relevant, cheap and indigenous materials for instruction; and assists clients in the preparation and production of
classroom instructional tools.
2.5.1	Recording Services. It attends to request for video and audio, and voice recording.
2.5.2	Documentation / Video Coverage. It caters video coverage for institutional, office, planned class activities and other special events.
2.5.3	Instructional Materials Services. It attends to request of the faculty for production of instructional materials for classroom use.
2.5.4	Photography Services. It provides AV support for specific lesson needs by way of graphics and photographic
materials.
2.6	Media Facilities. This program provides equipment and facilities to support the curricular and extracurricular activities of the faculty and students.
2.6.1	Media Satellite Program. This program provides satellite centers to include educational equipment for effective instruction.
2.6.2	Repair and Maintenance Program. It ensures that conditioned equipment and facilities are available.
2.6.3	Media External Networking. This program is intended to solicit assistance for acquisition on non−print materials.

Monday − Friday	7:00 am − 7:00 pm Saturday and Sunday	8:00 am − 12:00 nn Summer
Monday – Friday	8:00 am − 5:00 pm
Saturday	8:00 am − 12:00 nn

3.2	Request for services beyond office hours can be accommodated provided the requesting group will pay for the services rendered by the assisting staff.
3.3	All students and employees should leave their valid CJC ID at the media lending counter whenever they borrow any educational technology materials or equipment. Using another identification card is strictly not allowed.
3.4	The users of AV Hall must observe the following:
3.4.1	Eating is not allowed inside the AV Hall.
3.4.2	Audio Visual Hall can be booked for two consecutive meetings a week unless nobody puts in a request.
3.4.3	Requesting parties are required to fill out the form for AV Hall. No form, no reservation is observed.
3.4.4	Bookings must be made three days before the activity. The requesting group is responsible for the setting up or arranging  or returning of the furniture and equipment to its original set−up after use.
3.4.5	Damages to educational technology facilities and equipment will be charged to the requesting group.
3.4.6	The requesting group is required to inform the Edtech staff three days before the scheduled activity if it is cancelled, moved or postponed. The activity that will be held in the area without the supervision of an instructor
 
will not be allowed. The film will be evaluated before it will be viewed.
3.4.7	Use of pyrotechnics and the like are not allowed in the AV Hall.

3.5.3	The equipment should be picked−up and returned to the Edtech office by the borrower or authorized representative.
3.5.4	For practice activities, the requesting individual or group is allowed to use the equipment’s for one hour and may be renewed for another hour unless nobody puts in a request. Fines will be charged for not returning the equipment/materials on time: Php 10.00 for the first hour and Php 30.00 for the succeeding hours.
3.5.5	No equipment and materials should be brought outside the campus except those, which are related to community extension and spiritual animation that the College deems as integral part of its program.
3.5.6	Equipment shall not be transported to the classroom or other locations during rainy days to protect the unit from damages.
3.5.7	Delivered materials should be confirmed by the requesting group by signing the form.
3.5.8	Releasing of equipment in the evening during weekdays is until 7:00 p.m. Other days, it will be up to 5:00 p.m. only.
3.5.9	The equipment should not be left unattended. The borrower will be held liable for the loss or damage to the equipment arising from neglect, misuse or abuse.
3.6	Copyright Policy Implementing Guidelines:
3.6.1	No duplication of any copyrighted film, transparency, videotape or audiotape shall be made without permission from the copyright holder or other authorized person.
 
3.6.2	The College will assist faculty members and students in legally obtaining the desired materials or in securing permission to copy them.
3.6.3	The Center will record off−air and make available those programs for which permission to copy them has been legally or officially obtained. Under the existing copyright law, the recording normally includes:
a.	Programs dealing with news;
b.	Programs which are demonstrably otherwise not available for purchase or rental;
c.	Non−dramatic musical works and pictorial, graphic and sculptural works shown on public television;
d.	Programs or portions of programs the use of which qualifies for “Fair Use” classification under the copyright law;
e.	Absent extraordinary circumstances of which the College will follow the Guidelines for off−air recording of broadcast programming for educational purposes;
f.	The College will assist faculty and staff members in securing permission, when necessary, to record and use the desired materials;
g.	No audio or video of any live lecture, presentation, or performance of whatever kind will be made without the expressed permission from the producer and/or performer. This prohibition does not include the taping of events for the purpose of news gathering;
h.	No College audio−visual equipment may be used in contradiction of the above policies.

3.7	Fees and fines must be paid at the Finance Office.

D.	CJC-BR.	POLYCARP INSTITUTE FOR COMMUNITY DEVELOPMENT FOUNDATION

The Foundation is charged with the responsibility for planning, initiating, and coordinating all community−oriented projects and activities of the college and those of its units in the pursuance of the institutional mission and goals.
1.	OBJECTIVES
The Foundation effectively sustains its community development programs and services to:
 
1.1.	strengthen existing linkages and create new ones among various sectors;
1.2.	provide CJC students avenue for community engagements exposure;
1.3.	mobilize CJC personnel and alumni as collaborators in the delivery of community extension services; and
1.4.	design dual program directions: one for CJC community extension services and another for the management of funded projects.
2.	CORE PROGRAMS AND SERVICES

2.1.	Child and Youth Development Program− aimed to respond to the different faces of poverty through provision of integrated services as education, nutrition, health and sanitation for socially and economically disadvantaged families in both urban and rural areas.
This program provided opportunities for the CJC community to be responsibly involved in the socio−economic and cultural empowerment of the selected partners as a concrete way to demonstrate social concern. One of the major components of this program was the Children’s Assistance, Rehabilitation and Emancipation (CARE) which had culminated last May 2013. This program served urban poor communities in the city of Digos. Other components are the Br. Polycarp Scholarship Program or adopt−a Pupil Program, Medical Mission, PASKUNA Drive, and Emergency Assistance.
Existed for 29 years since 1984, the CARE project aimed to response to the different facets of child poverty as manifested by malnutrition, poor health and hygiene, social withdrawal and non−attendance in school. The project provided better opportunities for children, parents and families to access a better quality of life and sustained development through a capability building process. However, since it was officially graduated from the support of Child Fund Phil., this gave birth to Br. Polycarp Sponsorship Program.

Br. Polycarp Sponsorship
As an offshoot to the CARE project, this gives opportunities to the selected elementary and Highschool CARE beneficiaries to
 
continue their studies with educational support coming from the foundation. These children will receive school supplies, school bags, shoes, school uniforms and payment of their miscellaneous fees. They are also provided with capability building activities that could enhance their potentials and skills. Some of these capacity building activities are reading and numeracy, Story Telling, Personal Hygiene sessions, Handwashing and Proper tooth brushing and Value Formation. Parents are also given trainings and seminars like Responsible Parenthood, and Value Formation. A total of 140 children are enrolled in the program.

2.2.	Development Education Program− aims to address access to basic education particularly Early Childhood Education and Adult Education in remote communities, with particular bias to serving indigenous peoples (IPS).

Services provided	Target clientele/partners
Alternative Learning System	Out of School children and Youth in Davao del Sur/Davao Occidental
Alternative Learning System
The ALS−A&E program, in partnership with the Department of Education, facilitates the mainstreaming of Out−Of−School Youth and Children (OSY/OSC) and other school drop−outs in formal education by helping them to obtain certificates of completion in either elementary or secondary level. As a modified distance learning program where the identified learners undergo a modular course for 10 months covering different subject areas with corresponding learning competencies. Learners attend classes at least once a week for a whole day, mostly done on weekends or on other schedules as agreed by the learners and the Instructional Managers. However, in 2018 the school and the foundation focused on the review sessions for the learners since conduct of classes are taken care of by the Department of Education. At the end of the modular course, the learners take the national equivalency examination to get their equivalent competency certification.
2.3.	Micro, Small, Medium Enterprise Development Program− aims to provide technical assistance to the Micro, Small and Medium enterprises in Davao del Sur, and link them to potential partners
 
for financial and technical support to help strengthen and sustain their livelihoods, and capacitate them to become successful entrepreneurs.

Services provided	Target clientele/partners
Business	Registration Assistance through the Negosyo Center	Micro, small, medium enterprises (MSMEs) in Davao del Sur
Business Advisory Services	Micro, small, medium enterprises
(MSMEs) in Davao del Sur
Business	Information	and Advocacy	Micro, small, medium enterprises (MSMEs) in Davao del Sur
Capability Building	Identified MSMEs in Davao del Sur
Marketing of Products	


2.4.	Capability Development Program− aims to enhance capabilities of community partners and other stakeholders to sharpen their knowledge, skills and talents towards self and community empowerment.








Services provided	Target clientele/partners
Capability	Building	for CSOs	Urban and Rural poor communities in Davao del Sur/Davao Occidental composed of farmers, Indigenous People,  fisherfolks,  disadvantaged
groups: women, children and Youth

Comprehensive

2.5.	Community Welfare and Development Program− aims to provide support in partnership with the barangays and public schools in addressing problems on education, health and nutrition, and providing technical training support for barangay officials and workers and community members.

There are several activities that were implemented under this program. To name a few: Feeding Program for school children for 120 days, Reading and Numeracy Sessions, Brigada Eskwela, Provisions of School Supplies and Materials, Tree Planting and Parenting, Mangrove Planting, Coastal Clean−up, Financial Literacy for groups and associations, Provision of hygiene kits, capability building for barangay officials and teachers, capability building for students and parents, scholarship, and relief operations to affected families due to calamities.

PASKUNA Drive
A yearly gift−giving activity of Cor Jesu College community as their way of giving back and sharing their resources to the less fortunate families and communities. Primarily, beneficiaries are identified through the barangay/group, however these beneficiaries are visited by the staff of the foundation for validation and profiling. This happens every December of the year in celebration of Christmas.


Relief Operations
This is primarily given to victims of man−made or naturally−made calamities in a form of goods like rice, canned goods, sugar, milk, coffee, noodles, used shoes/clothes, etc. The goods are basically coming from the students, staff, faculty, administrators and other stakeholders of the institution. The goods are packed and distributed through the Br. Polycarp Foundation.

2.6.	Advocacy and Networking Program−aims to actively build partnerships with other groups and networks, and to get involved in the information and education campaign on specific concerns, particularly for the protection and management of environment and the promotion of peace and culture.
 
E.	SACRED HEART FORMATION AND MISSION OFFICE

The Sacred Heart Formation and Mission Office (SHFMO), directly under the Office of the President, ensures the realization of the Institution's vision−mission particularly in its missionary and spiritual aspect. It specifically strives for the integration of faith and life among the stakeholders of the Institution. It also carries out the mission of the Brothers of the Sacred Heart and three−fold mission of the school (Teaching, Worship / Animation and Service) with vigor and dynamism inspired by the spirituality of Compassion.
1.	OBJECTIVES
1.1.	To provide religious instruction in Cor Jesu College for greater appreciation and integration of the teachings of the Church;
1.2.	To provide other avenues for fuller expression of the faith through spiritual activities;
1.3.	To integrate the Catholic faith in the lives of the students, school personnel, alumni and parents through various spiritual services;
1.4.	To share the faith with other institutions outside of Cor Jesu College;
1.5.	To provide avenue for students who belong to other religions to express their faith inside the campus; and
1.6.	To provide catechetical resources to the students, school personnel and others.



2.	PROGRAMS
2.1.	Teaching. The teaching of Catholic religion leads the young to an enlightened and close union with Christ. It is a blend of religious studies and the dynamics of human development involving both instruction and formation as part of a life−long search for ultimate values and personal growth.
2.1.1.	Religious Instruction. A classroom−based Academic Program which promotes the fundamental initiation, learning and understanding of Christian Faith.
2.1.2.	College Religious Studies Subjects
 
RS 1	God’s Salvific Act
RS 2	Jesus and the Kingdom of God
RS 2	The  Church  and  Her  Celebrations:  Liturgy  and
Sacraments
RS 4	Christian Discipleship: Stewardship and Morality

2.1.3.	Catechetical and Resource Center. It is a resource center which provides instructional aids, books and other materials for religious instruction, liturgical services and animation activities.
2.2.	Worship. Prayer is essential to the making of our school genuinely Catholic. It is a celebration of life and love deepening and strengthening our relationship with the community and with God.
Individual and community prayer permeate our school in a natural way by becoming a regular part of the classrooms, of extra−curricular activities, of school celebrations, and especially of religion classes. Special programs of more intense prayer and sacramental life such as recollection and days of retreat will give our students and personnel the means to nurture their personal lives of faith.

2.2.1.	Institutional Masses. The SHFMO takes charge of the liturgy for fiesta, Holy Spirit, Thanksgiving Masses, and other institutional activities preceded by a mass.
2.2.2.	First Friday Devotion. The SHFMO leads the CJC community in praying the novena to the Sacred Heart of Jesus. It also takes charge of First Friday Masses;

1st Friday Mass	BED Elem & JHS	CJC Gym	8:00 am
1st Friday Mass	BED – SHS 11 & 12	CJC Gym	10:00 am
1st Friday Mass	College	Student,
Faculty & Staff	CJC Gym	3:00 pm

2.2.3.	Weekly Masses/Prayers. The SHFMO takes charge of the masses and other prayers both in the school and in the cathedral.
2.2.4.	Novena. The SHFMO leads the community in praying the novena as part of a feast of a particular saint, e.g. Feast of the Sacred Heart, patron saints of the BED, and etc.
 
2.2.5.	Adoration / Visit to the Blessed Sacrament. Every Thursday before 1st Friday, the SHFMO facilitates the adoration of the Blessed Sacrament at the School Chapel.
2.2.6.	Visit to the Blessed Sacrament. To provide a space for silence, prayer and reflection, the SHFMO prepares the School Prayer Room and encourages everyone to visit Jesus who is present in the tabernacle.
2.2.7.	Holy Rosary. The SHFMO initiates the celebration of the Holy Rosary Month. Different activities are done such as the launching of the Month of the Rosary, daily rosary, procession and culmination activities.
2.2.8.	Baptism. The SHFMO assists pupils/ students who want to avail of the Sacrament of Baptism. The office advises them on necessary things to prepare.
2.2.9.	Confirmation. The SHFMO attends to students who want to receive the Sacrament of Confirmation. The office arranges the holding of the ceremony either in the school or at the cathedral.
2.2.10.	Sacrament of Reconciliation. The SHFMO provides opportunities for anyone who would like to go for confession. The office invites a priest every Thursday before 1st Friday. This is simultaneous with the adoration of the Blessed Sacrament.
2.2.11.	Liturgical Season Activities. The SHFMO organizes and facilitates liturgical season activities such as the blessing of the Advent wreath, imposition of ashes, etc.


2.3.	Animation Activities
2.3.1.	Retreat. As a culminating activity of the spiritual formation program, the SHFMO facilitates a retreat for graduating pupils/students.
2.3.2.	Recollection. In coordination with RS teachers, the SHFMO facilitates recollection every year for those students who are taking RS subjects.
2.3.3.	Fellowship Days. In coordination with RS classes, the SHFMO spearheads the celebration of Fellowship Days. This activity is celebrated yearly as an integral part of RS classes.
 
2.3.4.	Vocation Festival. To promote vocations in the Church, the SHFMO organizes the Vocation Festival. This activity draws people from different states of life to come to CJC and share their life to students. This is also an opportunity for religious congregations to promote and recruit possible aspirants.
2.3.5.	BEC/SFC. The office supports the different Basic Ecclesial Communities inside the campus. It provides orientation and guidelines for doing BEC prayer meetings.
2.3.6.	Religious Clubs. The SHFMO encourages the students to join religious clubs/organizations. It provides training and ongoing−formation programs for their members.
2.3.7.	Professional Development Program. The SHFMO provides opportunities for career and spiritual development of its RS teachers and office staff by giving them animation activities and sending them for training and seminars.
2.4.	Pastoral Services. Service is the living out of what we teach and the giving of life to what we believe in. It is an expression of our spirituality of compassion and sense of mission. As a Catholic school, we lead the community especially the young, to be in solidarity with the suffering poor, in communion with the Local Church.
2.4.1.	Extension Program. The SHFMO extends its services beyond CJC. It helps other schools in the aspect of animation and liturgical services.
2.4.2.	Social Action Desk. In response to the social action ministry of the Church, the SHFMO initiates activities such as symposia, forums and rituals to awaken the awareness of the community regarding social issues. The office also spearheads collecting donations for victims of calamities.
2.4.3.	Prison Apostolate. The SHFMO extends its services to the inmates of the Provincial Jail Rehabilitation Center and Digos City Jail. Activities like Holy Eucharist, socio− program, and distribution of goods and food are being facilitated by the SHFMO staff, religious club members and other volunteers.
2.4.4.	Prayer Services for the Dead. In a spirit of solidarity to the bereaved family of CJC employees, students, alumni,
 
parents and friends, the SHFMO organizes a visit and a prayer for the dead.
2.4.5.	Wedding Assistance. The SHFMO assists CJC employees, students, alumni and friends in the preparation of the celebration of the Sacrament of Matrimony.
2.4.6.	Vocation Promotion. Aside from the Vocation Festival, the SHFMO helps in the promotion of vocation in the Church by helping vocation directors/directresses in their campaign and recruitment at CJC. It also displays posters and brochures at the SHFMO Bulletin.
2.4.7.	SAVE the Young Program. The CMO coordinates and assists the Brothers of the Sacred Heart Youth Ministry in its Save the Young Program. It also acts as contact base for the volunteers of the program.
F.	STUDENT SERVICES CENTER

The Student Services Center is responsible for providing adequate non− academic support programs and services for students. It generally provides and facilitates extra−curricular and co−curricular activities for the welfare and total development of students. Specifically, the Student Services Center ensures the following objectives:

1.	OBJECTIVES
1.1.	To provide avenues for information, orientation and forum for students in collaboration with other units or departments;
1.2.	To assist the developmental processes of the mental, emotional, physical and vocational well−being of students;
1.3.	To facilitate accreditation and re−accreditations of students’
associations or organizations;
1.4.	To cater and monitor on and off−campus student−initiated activities and/or institutional activities involving students;
1.5.	To initiate, organize and provide opportunities for trainings/seminar−workshops, sessions and formations for student leadership development;
1.6.	To ensure and monitor the implementation of the institutional norms and formative discipline of students;
1.7.	To organize, facilitate and hold activities, programs and performances relative to appreciation of culture and arts;
 
1.8.	To organize sports tournament on−campus and supervise participation to invitational games or athletic competitions in the provincial, regional and/or national level;
1.9.	To cater and provide services related to health and wellness for students and personnel; and
1.10.	To provide growth and developmental sessions and formations as support initiatives to student−scholars.


2.	PROGRAMS AND SERVICES

2.1.	STUDENT WELFARE PROGRAM. This refers to the basic programs and services that are necessary to serve the well−being of students. This includes Information and Orientation Services, Guidance and Counseling, Career and Placement and Student Handbook Development.
2.2.	STUDENT DEVELOPMENT PROGRAM. This refers to the programs and services designed for the exploration, enhancement and development of the student’s full potential for personal development, leadership and social responsibility through various institutional and/or student−initiated activities. This includes Student Organizational Development, Student Affairs and Activities, Student Council and Government, Student Discipline.
2.3.	INSTITUTIONAL STUDENT PROGRAMS AND SERVICES. These are
programs and services offered by the school to facilitate the delivery of essential services to the students that include Admission, Scholarship and Financial Assistance, Canteen Services, Health Services, Culture and Arts Development, and Sports Development.
2.4.	AUXILIARY SERVICES. In order to provide support for the effort of other units/offices to enhance their effectiveness and efficiency as well as quality of services being rendered to the students as well as other stakeholders, the Student Services Center has the following Auxiliary Services:
2.11.1.	Conduct students and administrators' forum;
2.11.2.	Facilitate the resolution of students' complaints and grievances against the school and the personnel;
2.11.3.	Facilitate formation session for student assistants and other non−academic scholars;
2.11.4.	Provide I.D. Validation stickers;
 
2.11.5.	Facilitate issuance of Certificate of Good Moral Character;
2.11.6.	Facilitate issuance of Parents' Consent;
2.11.7.	Cater Lost and Found Items; and
2.11.8.	Approval	of	written	and	on−air	or	public announcements
3.	REGULATIONS

3.1.	ID and Validation Sticker
3.1.1.	When the school ID is lost, the student is advised to report to the Student Services Center. He/she presents the affidavit of loss, and pay request form for the issuance of new ID;
3.1.2.	The issuance of validation stickers every semester must always be approved by the Director for Student Services;
3.1.3.	Student’s ID must be surrendered to the Student Services Center upon withdrawal from the College or after graduation;
3.1.4.	Security guards are under instructions to check students’ ID at all times upon entering the school; and
3.1.5.	Only bonafide students with valid ID may make use of the library and other school facilities.
3.2.	Certificate of Good Moral Character
Alumni and students who want to get a Certificate of Good Moral Character are required to get a request form at the Student Services Center and to be paid at the Cashier.


3.3.	Parent's Consent
Parent's consent letter is released to the school personnel or student only after the Director for Student Services has approved the activity of the group or organization.
3.4.	Lost and Found Items
3.4.1.	The Student Services Center receives report of lost materials and equipment and helps locate the same. The owner is required to state the circumstances of the loss; and
 
3.4.2.	Found valuables turned over to the Student Services Center are released only to the rightful owners upon presenting an ID. Signed authorization will be required in the absence of the owner.
3.5.	Other Regulations
3.5.1.	Records and documents for public use can be borrowed by the concerned person with the approval of the Director for Student Services. The borrower is required to sign in the record book for reference;
3.5.2.	To obtain clearance, alumni and former students must settle their financial obligations, submit requirements and return borrowed materials and equipment; and
3.5.3.	A complaint form is provided to anybody who wishes to file a complaint and is encouraged to write all the pertinent facts. He/She signs and submits the complaint to the Prefect of Discipline as early as possible for action.
4.	OFFICE HOURS

1:00 pm −  5:00 pm

5.	OFFICES AND UNITS UNDER THE UMBRELLA OF STUDENT SERVICES CENTER.

To be able to achieve the objectives of the Student Services Center as well as to successfully implement the programs and services, the Student Services Center, as a support unit has the following component offices and units:
5.1.	GUIDANCE AND COUNSELING CENTER (GCC)
The school Guidance and Counseling program is an integral part of the educational process. It refers to the range of learning
 
experiences which the school provides in response to the needs of the students and the available resources. This program is anchored on the American School Counseling Association (ASCA, 2012) National Model. This model is comprehensive in scope, preventive in design and developmental in nature.
Thus, program based on ASCA National Model brings school counselor together with one vision and one voice which creates unity and focus toward improving student achievement and supporting student development. Further, all guidance activities are rooted on “Compassion” the core value of the institution and designed to help students grow holistically, to think for themselves and others and develop their varied competencies needed to face the world.

In coordination and collaboration with the Student Services Center, The Guidance and Counseling Center plans for the optimum use of resources for the development of the students.

5.1.1.	GENERAL OBJECTIVE
To Promote the development of the whole person and encourages a lifestyle in students and the school community which integrates intellectual, emotional, physical, social, and vocational well−being.
5.1.2.	SPECIFIC OBJECTIVES
As a community of disciples, we, the Guidance and Counseling Personnel commit to:


a.	Academic Development
i.	Assist students to identity their aptitudes, interest, abilities and talents to help them assess and develop their potentials to the fullest;
ii.	Help students to acquire attitudes, knowledge, and skills that contribute to effective learning in school and across lifespan; and
iii.	Assist students to understand the relationship of academics to the world of work, and to life at home and in the community.
 
b.	Career Development
i.	Assist students to acquire the skills to investigate the world of wok in relation to knowledge of self and make informed career decisions;
ii.	Help the students to employ strategies to achieve future career goals with success and satisfaction;
iii.	Assist the students to understand the relationship between personal qualities, education, and the world of work; and
iv.	Assist the students to choose career and develop realistic vocation outlook, life goals and proper attitudes towards work.
c.	Personal/Social Development
i.	Help the students acquire the knowledge, attitudes, and interpersonal skills to help them understand and respect self and others;
ii.	Help the students make decisions, set goals, and take necessary action to achieve goals;
iii.	Help the students understand safety and survival skills;
iv.	Help the students develop the ability to make decisions wisely and to solve their problems independently; and
v.	Help parents understand the developmental needs of their children and work them in meeting the needs of their children in the school situation.

5.1.3.	PROGRAMS

a.	Counseling. This program assists the individual in understanding himself/herself better. It is one−on− one relationship with the counselor in which the counselee is helped to arrive at a certain decision. It may also be group counseling session where the members of the group, through the facilitation of the counselor, mutually help each other.
 
b.	Information Services. The purpose of this program is to deepen awareness of students, teachers and parents on the educational, vocational/occupation, personal and social concerns in relation to school life.

c.	Testing. The student's individual strengths and weaknesses in the areas of personality, aptitudes, interests, needs and job skills are assessed through the use of standardized tests. Test results are interpreted to the students for self−awareness, growth and development. Test interpretations are also made available in groups.
d.	Career Development. It assists students in their choice of career. This also equips them with appropriate knowledge, attitudes and these skills necessary in making progress both in their studies and occupation; facilitates them to discover their personal characteristics that make career−related difference; introduces them to many vocational opportunities; and assist them in entering, adjusting and progressing in their jobs.

e.	Job Placement and Follow-up. A seminar intended to assist graduating students that assists in their application letter writing, to practice interviewing, tips on how to sell oneself and help them enhance their CV’s in coping with employment crisis and for better career prospects. This service also supports students so they can prepare for job search process and connects employers and graduating students.

f.	Consultation. It is a service where counselors and school administrators/faculty/students/parents help each together to reach a desired goal most especially towards a holistic development of student.

g.	Follow-up. It is a service where counselors call students with behavioral problems, absences,
 
incomplete school works, failed subjects, and other problems pertaining studies for academic consultation. It also includes academic monitoring, and counselor−parent/guardian and counselor− teacher consultation to facilitate concerns affecting school performance and self−management.

h.	Referral. It is usually understood as the action taken by persons within the institution who see that a particular person needs counselor assistance (Villar, 2009). Thus, teachers, administrators, counselors, parents, and other students may refer student for counseling.

i.	Individual Inventory. It is a systematic way of the Guidance and Counseling Center to collect data about the students to identify the personalities and capacities of every client for future references.

j.	Research and Development. To obtain valid and reliable data needed for area of improvement and development, the Guidance Counselors conducts evaluation of its programs and services.







5.1.4.	Other Services
a.	Peer Counselors Program. Training workshop for student−peer−facilitators are conducted; aimed in developing their counseling and facilitating skills to establish effective self−awareness and peer relationship.
b.	Staff Development Program. It enriches the counselors' counseling skills and techniques and deepens their commitment and dedication to service.
 
c.	Parenting Program. It helps parents understand and accept their role as fist teacher of their children, improve their parenting skills and establish strong partnership with the school.
5.1.5.	Office Hours

Monday to Friday:	8:00 am − 12:00 nn
1:00 pm − 5:00 pm
Saturday:	8:00 am − 12:00 nn

5.2.	STUDENT AFFAIRS AND ACTVITIES

The Student Affairs and Activities as a component unit of the Student Services Center is responsible for the implementation of the Student Development programs, which are designed for the enhancement and deepening of social responsibility and leadership skills of the students. These programs include; Student Organizations and Activities, Leadership Training and Student Government. This unit also implements support programs and activities for the non−academic scholars particularly the student assistants, dance and music artists and athletes.
5.2.1.	OBJECTIVES
a.	To manage processes of recognition and accreditation, supervision and monitoring of student organizations including evaluation of student activities;
b.	To provide opportunities and training to develop and enhance leadership effectiveness in the personal level and student organizations;
c.	To ensure amplification of the students’ right to
govern themselves as student body; and
d.	To provide support services for the well−being of non− academic scholars.
5.2.2.	PROGRAMS
a.	Student Organizations and Activities. This program promotes dynamic student organizations that initiate  and  implement  student  development
 
activities. It includes the accreditation of student organizations, monitoring and evaluation of their approved activities.
b.	Leadership Training. This program offers opportunities to develop and enhance student’s leadership capabilities and effectiveness in the personal and organizational level. In CJC context, leadership is a developmental and an empowering process which focuses on the formation of “tatak Cor Jesian” such as; Christ−centered, community oriented, compassionate, disciplined, trusting & trustworthy, integrated, believes in human potentials, competent, available and service oriented.
c.	Student Government. This program refers to the recognition and supervision of the body government that conducts activities for the development of the whole studentry.
d.	Non-Academic Scholars Support Services. This program refers to the provision of developmental, psycho−social and capacity building activities to support the development of the non−academic scholars.

5.3.	STUDENT DISCIPLINE AND FORMATION
Student Discipline and Formation as a component unit of the Student Services Center is responsible for the implementation and monitoring of school policies on discipline, decorum, social norms and implementation formative intervention procedures.

5.3.1.	OBJECTIVES
a.	To maintain discipline inside the campus by ensuring the implementation of school policies;
b.	To orient students and school personnel on matters related to school discipline; and
c.	To inculcate the core value of the school.

5.3.2.	PROGRAMS
a.	Orientation on Student Discipline. This program refers to the provision of information and orientation of students on school policies related to discipline.
 
b.	Intervention on Student Absences. This program refers to the intervention process for referred students due to absences.
c.	Policy Monitoring. This program refers to the regular monitoring and implementation of institutional rules and norms stipulated in the Student Handbook.
d.	Formative Intervention. This program refers to the implementation of formative processes in disciplining students who have violated the school’s rules and policies.

5.3.3.	REGULATIONS
a.	Absences and Tardiness
i.	Students whose absences are due to illness are required to get a medical certificate or present an excuse letter signed by the parent to be confirmed by the School Clinic in charge before getting an excuse slip;
ii.	The students who reach the maximum number of absences as prescribed in this Handbook are required to see the Guidance Counselor for an interview before they can get a last−chance slip from the Prefect of Student Formation; and
iii.	There will be no issuance of last−chance slip one week before the final examinations.

b.	School Uniform
i.	The office gives uniform dispensation for a day or a semester to a student with considerable reasons to be approved by the DSS. The student must submit a letter of request to the Prefect of Student Formation; and
ii.	Students who are not in uniform should get a dispensation slip from the Prefect of Student Formation before they are allowed to enter the classroom.
5.4.	SCHOOL CLINIC
The school clinic is directly under the supervision of the Director of Students Services in providing adequate, sufficient, responsive
 
and proactive health and wellness development programs and services to the school community.

5.4.1.	OBJECTIVES
a.	To provide quality school−based health services incorporating Health Promotion and Primary Health Care;
b.	To promote, facilitate, and maintain physical, emotional and social heath to the school community;
c.	To give first aid and emergency treatment to pupils, students and school personnel;
d.	To equip the school community with knowledge on relevant health issues;
e.	To provide adequate medical and dental supplies;
f.	To keep the medical and dental record of students and school personnel; and
g.	To ensure the school's hygienic and sanitary condition.





5.4.2.	PROGRAMS AND SERVICES
a.	Medical and Dental Services. The School Clinic provides medical and dental check−ups for pupils and students throughout the school year. It makes recommendations for treatment to pupils and students that need medical and dental care. It issues campus leave form for students justifying their absence in their classes.
b.	Medicine for Temporary Relief. It provides medicines for temporary relief of illness to students and school personnel who need immediate attention while they are on campus or off campus school activities.
c.	Health Education Program and Services
i.	Water sampling
ii.	Fogging
iii.	Proactive Health education
iv.	Blood typing and letting
 
d.	Issuance of Medical Certificate. It issues medical certificates to pupils and students for school related activities.
e.	Confinement Space. It provides a bed for students and school personnel who are sick and need rest.
f.	Vital Signs, Height and Weight Monitoring. It provides free monitoring of blood pressure, height and weight of pupils, students and school personnel.

5.4.3.	REGULATIONS
a.	Clinic Hours:

Basic Education Department:
Monday to Friday:	7:30am − 5:00pm
College Department:
Monday to Friday:	 8:00am − 9:00pm Saturday and Sunday:	8:00am − 5:00pm

Tuesday:	10:00am − 12:00nn
Friday:	10:00am − 12:00nn


b.	Medical and Dental Services
i.	All students must present a valid ID upon requesting medicines and other health services;
ii.	Only patients are allowed to stay in the confinement area;
iii.	All students are encouraged to report to the clinic for medical and dental check−up on the day they are scheduled;
iv.	College students who avail of the medical and dental services must get a service slip from the clinic to be signed by the school physician or authorized staff.
 
v.	Service slip will only be signed if student has availed of the medical and dental services; and
vi.	A letter of request and names of students shall be required for request of medical and dental examinations for school related activities.
c.	Free Medicines for Temporary Relief
i.	The clinic provides medicines for temporary relief only; and
ii.	The clinic provides medicine for students who are in school and are sick.

d.	Minor Injuries
i.	The clinic provides first aid for minor injuries; and
ii.	The clinic also facilitates and organizes the first aid trainings of students and personnel
e.	Emergency Cases
i.	In emergency cases the nurse refers the students and personnel to hospitals and other health care agencies for further evaluation and management of illness or injuries sustained in school or out of school activities. Parents and guardians will be notified as soon as possible; and
ii.	Each student and school personnel is insured for one year, that is from June to May, expenses incurred due to hospitalization can be paid by the insurance provided that the cause is within the policies entered into by school and the insurance company. It holds through for death caused by accident. For details, the student or parents are advised to refer to the Director of Finance or Director of Students Services.
5.5.	SPORTS DEVELOPMENT
Sports unit is responsible for the sports development program of the institution, which is designed to develop physical fitness and wellness of students as well as of employees.

5.5.1.	PROGRAMS AND ACTIVITIES
 
a.	Varsity Recruitment Program. This program refers to the facilitation of recruitment, screening, try−outs and evaluation of athletes.
b.	Athletic Training Program. This program refers to facilitation of the training work−out, routines, exercises and practices to further enhance athletics skills and abilities of athletes.
c.	Sports Association Program. This program refers to the coordination with government and non− government agencies for the promotion of national, sectoral and cultural sports activities and developments
d.	Physical Fitness and Wellness Program. This program refers to the facilitation of sport activities for the development of physical fitness and wellness of students and personnel.

5.6.	MUSICAL ARTS
The Music Art unit is responsible for programs and activities designed to provide students with opportunities to develop and enhance talents, abilities and values for appreciation, promotion and conservation of national culture and multi−cultural heritage in terms of music.
Under the Student Services Center, provision for the development of talents and appreciation of cultural arts through music is facilitated by the Music Coordinator who is also the band master of the Red Ambassadors Band.

5.6.1.	PROGRAMS AND ACTIVITIES
a.	Band Recruitment Program. This program refers to recruitment, screening, audition and evaluation of talents or artists.
b.	Music Workshops. This program refers to the Facilitation of workshops, skills development trainings and practices for further enhancement of musical talents and abilities.
c.	Musical Exposure Program. This program refers to musical performances for cultural arts appreciation whether on campus, during school activities and
 
celebrations or off−campus as invitational or marketing purposes.
d.	Culture and Arts Network Program. This refers to the coordination with the City or Provincial tourism on culture and arts for partnership and for representation of the CJC’s contribution to the development of tourism programs of the City or Province.
5.7.	CANTEEN SERVICES
Canteen Services of Cor Jesu College is managed by a designated canteen in−charge. The business aspect of the canteen in terms of rentals of concessionaires, permits, electric and water consumption and the like is under the finance office. The monitoring aspect of the canteen services in terms of sanitation of the place, foods and food servers is managed by the Student Services Center through the school clinic.
5.7.1.	OBJECTIVES
a.	To sell nutritious ready−to−eat food to the students and school personnel; and
b.	To maintain clean and orderly food service areas.

5.7.2.	PROGRAMS AND SERVICES
a.	Catering Services
b.	Fast Food Services
c.	Grocery

5.7.3.	REGULATIONS
a.	General Rules
i.	Cleanliness and orderliness must always be maintained inside the Canteen. Refuse must be thrown into the proper trashcans;
ii.	Electric fans and lights must be switched off when they are not being used;
iii.	All customers are required to minimize their noise while they are inside the canteen;
iv.	The canteen area is for eating purposes only; and
v.	Concessioners are required to strictly follow the policies and procedures for canteen services crafted by the Student Services Center.
 
b.	Fast Food Services
i.	Customers must queue while waiting to be served; and
ii.	The canteen personnel must immediately clean the table after the customers leave.

c.	School Personnel Food Service Area
i.	This area is for school personnel and for visitors only; and
ii.	The lavatory inside the school personnel service area is only used for drinking and for washing of hands.

G.	EXTERNAL AND ALUMNI AFFAIRS OFFICE
The office is responsible for the implementation of the programs and services for the Alumni and other outside stakeholders of the College.

1.	OBJECTIVES
1.1.	To function as the liaison office between the alumni and the school;
1.2.	To assist in the organization of various alumni groups in order to extend the partnership of alumni with the school in the latter’s mission and vision; and
1.3.	To develop programs that are aligned with the school’s mission
and vision for alumni involvement.

2.	PROGRAMS AND SERVICES
2.1.	Social Concerns. The office develops programs related to the social mission of the school to help those who are in need of hope by coordinating with other units to provide aid during calamities, facilitate scholarships and other financial assistance. It also develops programs to enhance the alumni’s stewardship role in society by such actions as participating in environmental protection activities, cultural development, and good citizenship.
2.2.	Spiritual Enhancement. The office, in coordination with other school units, facilitates spiritual activities for the alumni in order to establish closer relationship with God, guided by the charism of the Brothers of the Sacred Heart.
2.3.	Social Development. The office, in collaboration with the various alumni groups, establishes the spirit of belongingness and
 
camaraderie among alumni and strengthens their bonding with one another through homecomings, sports and other activities.
2.4.	Organizational Assistance. The office provides assistance to the alumni as an organized body such as the registration and operation of the Cor Jesu College Alumni Association, Inc. to ensure the continuation of its juridical personality. The office maintains the physical headquarters of the association and assists in its day−to−day functions and facilitates policy− formulation and execution as warranted.

SECTION XII.
Institutional Services
A.	THE FINANCE OFFICE

The Office of Finance is responsible for the custody and administration of the funds of the College.

1.	OBJECTIVES
1.1.	To plan, implement and pursue a program of effective and efficient managing of the financial affairs of the College; and
1.2.	To develop a system of control and evaluation of all activities relating to financial operations.

2.	REGULATIONS
2.1.	All financial transaction must be course through the Office of Finance.
2.2.	The tuition fees and other fees are published and posted on the Finance Bulletin Board before and during enrolment periods.
2.3.	Payment of Fees. At the start of every semester, every student is required to pay a down payment of not less than ₱2,500.00 or thirty percent (30%) of the total assessment for the semester. Each student is also required to follow the schedule of payments which is pre requisite for the issuance of examination permit. It is assumed that the remaining accounts of old students are fully settled before they are allowed to enrol again. Regular charges include the following:
2.3.1.	Tuition
2.3.2.	Miscellaneous Fees
 
2.3.3.	Laboratory fees
2.3.4.	Other CHED approved fees

2.4.	Payments of fees are made according to the following arrangement: Upon registration, one−fourth of the total assessment shall be paid, but in no case shall it be less than Two Thousand Pesos (₱2,000.00). The balance is to be equally divided into four monthly installments.
2.5.	Discount on Full Payments during Enrollment. Student who pays the total assessment in full upon registration will be given 5% discount on tuition fees. The discount is not applicable to foreign students.
2.6.	Family Discount. A discount is given to a family under education aid benefits based on tuition only. The three (3) discounts to be granted are as follows:

No. of children enrolled	Discount for the last student
admitted
3	20% for 3rd child
4	30% for 4th child
5 or more	40% each in excess of 5

2.7.	Scholarships
2.7.1.	The College, through the Financial Assistance Program, offers scholarships such as student grants, academic, band and athletic scholarships.
2.7.2.	Honor Students. CJC is granting scholarship to students who graduated with honors in senior high school. The specifications are as follows:

Honors	Scholarship Grants
Top 1	100% tuition
Top 2	50% tuition
Top 3 – top 7	25% tuition
Battle of Academic Wizard
Winners	Depending on results
Dean’s lister	Depending on Grades
Athletic Scholars	21 units plus miscellaneous
fees
 
Note: CJC will ask for a certification from the registrar where the student finished his/her senior high school indicated his/her specific rank.
2.8.	Charge for Withdrawal. A student who transfers or otherwise withdraws in writing within two weeks after the beginning of classes and who has already paid the pertinent tuition and other school fees in full or on any length longer than one month may be charged on the following terms:
2.8.1.	(10%) ten percent of the total amount due for the term if he/she withdraws within the first week of classes;
2.8.2.	(20%) twenty percent if within the second week of classes, regardless of whether or not he/she has actually attended the classes;
2.8.3.	(50%) fifty percent if within the 4th week of classes regardless of whether or not he/she has actually attended the classes;
2.8.4.	(70%) seventy percent if within the 6th week of classes regardless of whether or not he/she has actually attended the classes; and
2.8.5.	(100%) one−hundred percent or all the school fees be charged if he/she withdraws any time after the 100 days of classes.
2.9.	Change of Program Fee. A fee is required for each change of program made by the student after he/she is officially enrolled in the amount of two hundred pesos (200.00) only.
2.10.	Late Registration Fee. A returning student who enrolls after the deadline set for registration shall be required to pay P100.00
2.11.	Family Account. The unpaid accounts if any, of a brother(s) and/or sister(s) who enrolled in CJC shall be considered a family account due and payable within 30 days.
2.12.	Students with Educational Aid from any private or government agencies are required to present letters of authorization from the employing/sponsoring organization to accept payment of charges through the specific channel (on−line banking)
2.13.	Dishonored Checks. Check payments made by the students that are dishonored by the bank due to reasons such as NO SUFFICIENT FUNDS, ACCOUNT CLOSED or STOPPED PAYMENT
shall be charged back to the student together with a penalty
 
equivalent to 5% of the face value of the check or P200 whichever is higher.
2.14.	Special Subject Requested by students for classes not offered in a particular semester, are allowed to be opened with a minimum of twenty−two (22) students enrolled in the subject, otherwise the enrollees will equally pay the remaining slot, as determined by the Finance Officer−in−charge.
